        <meta property="og:url" content="https://pubs.acs.org/doi/full/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408"><meta property="og:title" content="Rational Design of Quasi-1D Multicore–Shell MnSe@N-Doped Carbon Nanorods as High-Performance Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries"><meta property="og:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/asset/images/acs.nanolett.4c01408.social.jpeg_v03"><meta property="og:description" content="Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered one of the promising candidates for energy storage devices due to the low cost and low redox potential of sodium. However, their implementation is hindered by sluggish kinetics and rapid capacity decay caused by inferior conductivity, lattice deterioration, and volume changes of conversion-type anode materials. Herein, we report the design of a multicore–shell anode material based on manganese selenide (MnSe) nanoparticle encapsulated N-doped carbon (MnSe@NC) nanorods. Benefiting from the conductive multicore–shell structure, the MnSe@NC anodes displayed prominent rate capability (152.7 mA h g–1 at 5 A g–1) and long lifespan (132.7 mA h g–1 after 2000 cycles at 5 A g–1), verifying the essence of reasonable anode construction for high-performance SIBs. Systematic in situ microscopic and spectroscopic methods revealed a highly reversible conversion reaction mechanism of MnSe@NC. Our study proposes a promising route toward developing advanced transition metal selenide anodes and comprehending electrochemical reaction mechanisms toward high-performance SIBs."><meta property="og:type" content="Article"><meta property="og:site_name" content="ACS Publications"><meta name="twitter:card" content="summary_large_image"><meta name="twitter:site" content="@ACSPublications"><meta name="twitter:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/asset/images/acs.nanolett.4c01408.social.jpeg_v03">

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/wro/1122814~thiss-ds.js" async="" nonce="93187f3f89a3075b-SJC"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="93187f3f89a3075b-SJC">

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            timeout: 5000,

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
            },
            retrieveEntity: function (ms) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                if (ms == undefined || ms === '') {
                    ms = this.timeout;
                }

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res.data);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('failed to retrieve entity from local storage: ' + err);
                        });
                    // Set up the timeout
                    setTimeout(function () {
                        reject('Promise timed out ' + ms + ' ms');
                    }, ms);
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage due to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {
                            doi: doi,
                            entityid: entityId,
                            entityTitle: entityTitle,
                            eventGroupKey: '0efc2e75-5b05-498e-9fea-4273d8fa9ba3'
                        }

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    }).fail(function (status) {
                        return reject(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (i = 0; i < allSsoInstitutions.length; i++) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        if(allSsoInstitutions.length === 0 && true){
                            self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, null, null)
                                .then(function () {
                                    console.log('No Entity found');
                                }, function (err) {
                                    console.log('failed to get the none entity status' ,err);
                                });
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            }).catch(function (err) {
                                reject(err);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();

                    if ($('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').length > 0) {
                        let institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox = $('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').get(0);
                        if (!$(institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox).is(":checked")) {
                            return;
                        }
                    }

                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

src="/specs/products/achs/releasedAssets/public/mathjax-0a9852ad89643b94fe5099b753f6a294/MathJax.js?config=TeX-AMS-MML_HTMLorMML"></script><script type="text/x-mathjax-config;executed=true">MathJax.Hub.Config({
            menuSettings: {
                zoom: "Click",
                zscale: "150%"
            },
            SVG: {
                fonts: ["STIX-Web"],
                linebreaks: { automatic: true },
            },
            "HTML-CSS": {
                fonts: ["STIX"],
                linebreaks: { automatic: true },
                scale: 90,
            },
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("mml Jax Ready", function () {
            var MML = MathJax.ElementJax.mml;
            MML.mi.prototype.setTeXclass = function (prev) {
                this.getPrevClass(prev);
                return this;
            };
            MML.mfrac.Augment({
                setTeXclass: function (prev) {
                    this.getPrevClass(prev);
                    for (var i = 0, m = this.data.length; i < m; i++) {
                        if (this.data[i]) this.data[i].setTeXclass();
                    }
                    return this;
                }
            });
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("SVG Jax Ready", function () {
            var FONT = MathJax.OutputJax.SVG.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-Web-variant"] || MathJax.OutputJax.SVG.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-variant"];
            delete MathJax.ElementJax.mml.mo.prototype.remapChars['°'];
            if (FONT) {
                FONT.remap[0xB0]= [0x25E6, "normal"];
                FONT.remap[0x2A]= [0x2217, "normal"];
            }

        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("MathML Jax Ready", function () {
            var PARSE = MathJax.InputJax.MathML.Parse;
            var ADD = PARSE.prototype.AddChildren;
            PARSE.Augment({
                AddChildren: function (mml, node) {
                    ADD.call(this, mml, node);
                    if (mml.type === 'mrow') {
                        var first = mml.data[0], last = mml.data[mml.data.length-1];
                        if (mml.open && !mml.data[0].Get('stretchy')) delete mml.open;
                        if (mml.close && !mml.data[mml.data.length - 1].Get('stretchy')) delete mml.close;
                    }
                }
            });
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("HTML-CSS Jax Ready", function () {
            var HTMLCSS = MathJax.OutputJax['HTML-CSS'];
            var DELIMITERS = HTMLCSS.FONTDATA.DELIMITERS;
            var FONT = HTMLCSS.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-variant"] || HTMLCSS.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-Web-variant"]

            var MML = MathJax.ElementJax.mml;

            MML.mrow.Augment({
              _HTMLlineBreaks: MML.mrow.prototype.HTMLlineBreaks,
              HTMLlineBreaks: function (span) {

                if (this.parent.linebreakContainer && this.Get("display") === "inline") return false;
                return this._HTMLlineBreaks(span);
              }
            });


            DELIMITERS[0x0305] = {dir: "H", alias: 0x00AF};
            DELIMITERS[0x033F] = {dir: "H", alias: 0x003D};
            DELIMITERS[0x20E1] = {dir: "H", alias: 0x2194};

            if (FONT) {
                FONT.remap[0xB0]= [0x25E6, "normal"];
                FONT.remap[0x2A]= [0x2217, "normal"];
            }

            delete MathJax.ElementJax.mml.mo.prototype.remapChars['°'];
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("HTML-CSS multiline Ready", function () {
            var HTMLCSS = MathJax.OutputJax["HTML-CSS"];
            var MML = MathJax.ElementJax.mml;
            var PENALTY = MML.mbase.prototype.HTMLlinebreakPenalty;

            MML.msqrt.Augment({
                linebreakContainer: false,
                HTMLbetterBreak: function () {return false}
            });
            MML.mroot.Augment({
                linebreakContainer: false,
                HTMLbetterBreak: function () {return false}
            });
            MML.mfrac.Augment({
                linebreakContainer: false,
                HTMLbetterBreak: function () {return false}
            });
            MML.mspace.Augment({
                defaultDef: {
                    indentalign: MML.INDENTALIGN.AUTO,
                    indentshift: "0",
                    indenttarget: "",
                    indentalignfirst: MML.INDENTALIGN.INDENTALIGN,
                    indentshiftfirst: MML.INDENTSHIFT.INDENTSHIFT,
                    indentalignlast: MML.INDENTALIGN.INDENTALIGN,
                    indentshiftlast: MML.INDENTSHIFT.INDENTSHIFT
                },
                HTMLbetterBreak: function (info,state) {
                    if (info.values && info.values.id === this.spanID) {return false}
                    var values = this.getValues(
                        "linebreak",
                        "indentalign","indentshift",
                        "indentalignfirst","indentshiftfirst",
                        "indentalignlast","indentshiftlast"
                    );
                    var linebreakValue = values.linebreak;
                    if (!linebreakValue || this.hasDimAttr()) {
                        linebreakValue = MML.LINEBREAK.AUTO;
                    }
                    var W = info.scanW, span = this.HTMLspanElement(), w = span.bbox.w;
                    if (span.style.paddingLeft) {w += HTMLCSS.unEm(span.style.paddingLeft)}
                    if (W - info.shift === 0) {return false} // don't break at zero width
                    var offset = HTMLCSS.linebreakWidth - W;

                    if (state.n === 0 && (values.indentshiftfirst !== state.VALUES.indentshiftfirst ||
                        values.indentalignfirst !== state.VALUES.indentalignfirst)) {
                        var align = this.HTMLgetAlign(state,values),
                            shift = this.HTMLgetShift(state,values,align);
                        offset += (info.shift - shift);
                    }

                    var penalty = Math.floor(offset / HTMLCSS.linebreakWidth * 1000);
                    if (penalty < 0) {penalty = PENALTY.toobig - 3*penalty}
                    penalty += info.nest * PENALTY.nestfactor;

                    var linebreak = PENALTY[linebreakValue]||0;
                    if (linebreakValue === MML.LINEBREAK.AUTO && w >= PENALTY.spacelimit &&
                        !this.mathbackground && !this.background)
                    {linebreak = [(w+PENALTY.spaceoffset)*PENALTY.spacefactor]}
                    if (!MathJax.Object.isArray(linebreak)) {
                        if (linebreak || offset >= 0) {penalty = linebreak * info.nest}
                    } else {penalty = Math.max(1,penalty + linebreak[0] * info.nest)}

                    if (penalty >= info.penalty) {return false}
                    info.penalty = penalty; info.values = values; info.W = W; info.w = w;
                    values.lineleading = state.VALUES.lineleading;
                    values.linebreakstyle = "before"; values.id = this.spanID;
                    return true;
                }
            });


            
            PENALTY.goodbreak = [-400];

        });</script><style type="text/css">.MathJax_Hover_Frame {border-radius: .25em; -webkit-border-radius: .25em; -moz-border-radius: .25em; -khtml-border-radius: .25em; box-shadow: 0px 0px 15px #83A; -webkit-box-shadow: 0px 0px 15px #83A; -moz-box-shadow: 0px 0px 15px #83A; -khtml-box-shadow: 0px 0px 15px #83A; border: 1px solid #A6D ! important; display: inline-block; position: absolute}

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="93187f3f89a3075b-SJC">
var dfpReady = false;
$(document).ready(function() {
    // var journalTitle = 'nano_letters';
    var taxonomyKeywords = $('.article_header-taxonomy');
    var articleKeyword = $('meta[name="keywords"]');
    var articleTitle = $('meta[name="dc.Title"]');
    var articleDescription = $('meta[name="dc.Description"]');
    var abstractKeyword = $('p.articleBody_abstractText:contains("Keywords: ")');
    var searchTerms = [];

    if (taxonomyKeywords.length > 0) {
        $(taxonomyKeywords).children(".rlist--inline").children("li").each(function() {
            searchTerms.push($(this).text());
        });
    }
    else if (articleKeyword.length > 0) { 
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleKeyword.prop('content').split(', '));
    }
    else if (abstractKeyword.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(abstractKeyword.text().split("Keywords: ")[1].split('; '));
    }
    else if (articleDescription.length > 0) {
        $(articleDescription).each(function() {
            articleDescriptionKeywords = $(this).prop('content');
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/.,/g,"");
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/\s{2,}/g," ");
            searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleDescriptionKeywords.split(' '));
        });
    }

    if (articleTitle.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleTitle.prop('content').split(' '));
    }

    googletag.cmd.push(function() {
        var mappingLeader = googletag.sizeMapping().
        addSize([750, 200], [728, 90]). 
        addSize([0, 0], [320, 50]).
        build();
        //leaderboard
        googletag.defineSlot('/8868/journal/nano_letters/article', [728, 90], 'dfp-journal-article-leaderboard').defineSizeMapping(mappingLeader).setTargeting('location', 'leaderboard1').setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //recommend
        googletag.defineSlot("/8868/journal/nano_letters/article", [1, 1], "dfp-journal-article-recommend").setTargeting("ntvPlacement", ["1100167"]).setTargeting("location", "recommend").setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //googletag.pubads().enableSingleRequest();
        googletag.pubads().collapseEmptyDivs();
        googletag.pubads().setTargeting('inst',dartInstitutionType).setTargeting('memb',dartMember);
        googletag.pubads().addEventListener("slotRenderEnded", function(event) {
            console.log(event.slot.getSlotElementId() + " isEmpty: " + event.isEmpty + " | creative id: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            if((event.isEmpty === false) && (event.slot.getSlotElementId() != "dfp-journal-article-recommend")) {
                $("#" + event.slot.getSlotElementId()).parents(".advertisement").slideDown();
                console.log("ad display: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            }
            // else {
            //     console.log("no ad found");
            // }
        });
        googletag.enableServices();
        dfpReady = true;
    });
});
</script>

class="article--latest"><div class="figure-viewer"><div class="figure-viewer_row"><div class="figure-viewer_col loop-trap"><div aria-live="polite" aria-atomic="true" class="figure-viewer_modal"><a <script nonce="93187f3f89a3075b-SJC">
$(function() {
    var serialCode = "nalefd";
    var books = ["reagents", "symposium", "advances", "medichemreviews", "styleguide"]
    if(books.includes(serialCode) === false) {
        // default click action
        $("[data-id]").on("mousedown", function(e) {
            var currentClickID = $(this).attr("data-id");

            if(currentClickID.includes("_hover") === false) {
                if(currentClickID.match("^article_") && !currentClickID.match("^article_abstract_CC")) {   
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Rational Design of Quasi-1D Multicore–Shell MnSe@N-Doped Carbon Nanorods as High-Performance Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                }
            }
        });
        
        // Access Management icons hover
        var articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        var articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent === false) {
                articleAccessManagementIconHover = true;
                var articleAccessManagementHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleAccessManagementIconHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Rational Design of Quasi-1D Multicore–Shell MnSe@N-Doped Carbon Nanorods as High-Performance Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408", "Article_Element": articleAccessManagementHover });
    
                        articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        });
    
        // articleRightsPermissionsLink hover
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent === false) {
                articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = true;
                var articleRightsHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Rational Design of Quasi-1D Multicore–Shell MnSe@N-Doped Carbon Nanorods as High-Performance Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408", "Article_Element": articleRightsHover });
    
                        articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        });
    
        // Author hover
        var articleAuthorHover = false
        var articleAuthorHoverEvent = false
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if((articleAuthorHoverEvent === false) && ($(this).parent().hasClass("view-affs") === false)) {
                articleAuthorHover = true;
                var authorInfoHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAuthorHover === true) && (articleAuthorHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Rational Design of Quasi-1D Multicore–Shell MnSe@N-Doped Carbon Nanorods as High-Performance Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408", "Article_Element": authorInfoHover });
    
                        articleAuthorHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAuthorHover = false;
        });
    
        // CC License hover
        var articleAbstractCCHover = false
        var articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = false
        var articleDrawerCCHover = false
        var articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = false
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if($(this).attr("data-id")) {
                if(($(this).attr("data-id") === "article_drawer_CC-License") && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleDrawerCCHover = true;
                    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleDrawerCCHover === true) && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Rational Design of Quasi-1D Multicore–Shell MnSe@N-Doped Carbon Nanorods as High-Performance Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408", "Article_Element": "article_drawer_CC-License_hover" });
    
                            articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
                else if(($(this).attr("data-id").match("^article_abstract_CC")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleAbstractCCHover = true;
    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Rational Design of Quasi-1D Multicore–Shell MnSe@N-Doped Carbon Nanorods as High-Performance Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                            articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
            }
            else if(($(this).hasClass("article__cc-license__link")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = true;
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Rational Design of Quasi-1D Multicore–Shell MnSe@N-Doped Carbon Nanorods as High-Performance Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                        articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            if(articleAbstractCCHover === true) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = false;
            }
            if(articleDrawerCCHover = true) {
                articleDrawerCCHover = false;
            }
        });
        
        // show recommeneded click delay
        var intervalCount = 0;
        var showRecommendedInterval = setInterval(function() {
            intervalCount += 100;
            if($(".show-recommended__wrapper .show-recommended").length > 0) {
                clearInterval(showRecommendedInterval);
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowMore']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Rational Design of Quasi-1D Multicore–Shell MnSe@N-Doped Carbon Nanorods as High-Performance Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowLess']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Rational Design of Quasi-1D Multicore–Shell MnSe@N-Doped Carbon Nanorods as High-Performance Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
            }
        }, 100);
    }
});
</script>

hidden"><div data-badge-details="right" data-badge-type="donut" data-hide-no-mentions="false" data-condensed="true" class="altmetric-embed"></div></div></div><div class="articleMetrics_count"><h2>Citations</h2><div class="articleMetrics-val"><a href="#citeThis" class="internalNav">5</a></div></div></div></div><div class="articleMetrics_about"><div class="base dropBlock"><a href="#" data-db-target-for="aboutArticleMetrics" aria-describedby="about-article-metrics" class="article_aboutLink">Learn about these metrics</a><div data-db-target-of="aboutArticleMetrics" id="about-article-metrics" class="dropBlock__holder"><button class="articleMetrics_close"> <i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-close_thin"></i><span class="sr-only">close</span></button><p>Article Views are the COUNTER-compliant sum of full text article downloads since November 2008 (both PDF and HTML) across all institutions and individuals. These metrics are regularly updated to reflect usage leading up to the last few days.</p><p>Citations are the number of other articles citing this article, calculated by Crossref and updated daily.<a href="https://www.crossref.org/services/cited-by/"> Find more information about Crossref citation counts.</a></p><p>The Altmetric Attention Score is a quantitative measure of the attention that a research article has received online. Clicking on the donut icon will load a page at altmetric.com with additional details about the score and the social media presence for the given article. Find more information on<a href="https://help.altmetric.com/support/solutions/articles/6000233311-how-is-the-altmetric-attention-score-calculated"> the Altmetric Attention Score and how the score is calculated.</a></p></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="article_abstract"><div class="article_abstract-title" id="Abstract" tabindex="0"><h2>Abstract</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div><div class="article_abstract-content hlFld-Abstract" id="abstractBox" property="description"><figure id="_i1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure article_abstract-img"><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img class="inline-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/asset/images/medium/nl4c01408_0006.gif" alt="" id="tgr1" property="image" style="width:405px; height:275px"></button><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/asset/images/large/nl4c01408_0006.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408&amp;id=_i1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="articleBody_abstractText">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered one of the promising candidates for energy storage devices due to the low cost and low redox potential of sodium. However, their implementation is hindered by sluggish kinetics and rapid capacity decay caused by inferior conductivity, lattice deterioration, and volume changes of conversion-type anode materials. Herein, we report the design of a multicore–shell anode material based on manganese selenide (MnSe) nanoparticle encapsulated N-doped carbon (MnSe@NC) nanorods. Benefiting from the conductive multicore–shell structure, the MnSe@NC anodes displayed prominent rate capability (152.7 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 5 A g<sup>–1</sup>) and long lifespan (132.7 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> after 2000 cycles at 5 A g<sup>–1</sup>), verifying the essence of reasonable anode construction for high-performance SIBs. Systematic <i>in situ</i> microscopic and spectroscopic methods revealed a highly reversible conversion reaction mechanism of MnSe@NC. Our study proposes a promising route toward developing advanced transition metal selenide anodes and comprehending electrochemical reaction mechanisms toward high-performance SIBs.</p></div><div class="article__cc-license"><div class="article__cc-license__body"><p class="article__cc-license__para">This publication is licensed under the terms of your
                            institutional subscription.
                            <a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D11349%26pageCount%3D9%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DLei%2BWang%252C%2BFei%2BHuang%252C%2BXinmei%2BSong%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D24%26issueNum%3D37%26contentID%3Dacs.nanolett.4c01408%26title%3DRational%2BDesign%2Bof%2BQuasi-1D%2BMulticore%25E2%2580%2593Shell%2BMnSe%2540N-Doped%2BCarbon%2BNanorods%2Bas%2BHigh-Performance%2BAnode%2BMaterial%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26numPages%3D9%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1530-6984%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Dnalefd%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D11357%26publicationDate%3DSeptember%2B2024" class="link--bold">Request reuse permissions.</a></p></div></div><span class="hidden" property="publisher">ACS Publications</span><div class="article_header-article-copyright">Copyright © 2024 American Chemical Society</div><div class="article_header-footer-right"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone7" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone7"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div><div class="article__tags article__tags--subjects"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Subjects</h3><div tabindex="0" class="article__tags__tooltip"><div aria-describedby="tooltip-subjects" class="article__tags__icon"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are subjects</span></div><p id="tooltip-subjects" role="tooltip" class="article__tags__diff">
                                        Article subjects are automatically applied from the ACS Subject Taxonomy and describe the scientific concepts and themes of the article.</p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291517&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Batteries"> Batteries </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291371&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Electrodes"> Electrodes </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291553&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Granular materials"> Granular materials </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=292316&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Transition metals"> Transition metals </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=292275&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Transmission electron microscopy"> Transmission electron microscopy </a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article__tags article__tags--keywords hlFld-Abstract"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Keywords</h3><div class="article__tags__tooltip" tabindex="0"><div class="article__tags__icon" aria-describedby="tooltip-keywords"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are keywords</span></div><p class="article__tags__diff" id="tooltip-keywords" role="tooltip">
                        Article keywords are supplied by the authors and highlight key terms and topics
                        of the paper.
                    </p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Mnse&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_MnSe">MnSe</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Nitrogen-doped+Nanoporous+Carbon&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_Nitrogen-doped%20nanoporous%20carbon">Nitrogen-doped nanoporous carbon</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Sodium-ion+Batteries&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_Sodium-ion%20batteries">Sodium-ion batteries</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Anode+Material&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_Anode%20material">Anode material</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Conversion+Reaction+Mechanism&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_Conversion%20reaction%20mechanism">Conversion reaction mechanism</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody" style="width: 384px;"><p class="first">Lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) have been widely applied in electric vehicles and portable devices. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1 ref2 ref3 ref4" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref1 ref2 ref3 ref4" aria-label="reference 1 to 4">(1−4)</a> However, the increasing cost of LIBs caused by a shortage of lithium resource leads to a failure to meet the growing demands, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref5" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref5" aria-label="reference 5">(5)</a> thus global researchers are urgently seeking new types of rechargeable batteries. Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are one of the most promising candidates for supplementing LIBs due to the high resource abundance and low redox potential of sodium. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref6 ref7 ref8" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref6 ref7 ref8" aria-label="reference 6 to 8">(6−8)</a> However, the larger radius of Na<sup>+</sup> ions (1.02 Å) compared to Li<sup>+</sup> ions (0.76 Å) results in severe volume expansion and slow kinetics during the charging–discharging process, resulting in rapid capacity decay and poor rate performance. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref9 ref10 ref11" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref9 ref10 ref11" aria-label="reference 9 to 11">(9−11)</a></p><p>To address the aforementioned issues, significant efforts have been made to identify suitable anode materials for SIBs, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref12 ref13 ref14 ref15 ref16 ref17" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref12 ref13 ref14 ref15 ref16 ref17" aria-label="reference 12 to 17">(12−17)</a> including carbon materials such as hard carbon <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref18" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref18" aria-label="reference 18">(18)</a> and phosphorus-doped carbon, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref19" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref19" aria-label="reference 19">(19)</a> alloy-based materials such as Sn@C nanoboxes <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref20" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref20" aria-label="reference 20">(20)</a> and microsized gray tin <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref21" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref21" aria-label="reference 21">(21)</a> and transition metal chalcogenides materials such as ZnS-NC/SnS<sub>2</sub> nanocages <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref13" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref13" aria-label="reference 13">(13)</a> and Fe<sub>7</sub>Se<sub>8</sub> nanoparticles. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref22" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref22" aria-label="reference 22">(22)</a> Among these options, manganese selenide (MnSe), a typical transition metal selenide (TMS), is of great potential due to its high specific capacity, low cost, and environmental compatibility. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23 ref24" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref23 ref24" aria-label="reference 23 and 24">(23,24)</a> Furthermore, MnSe has higher conductivity and faster reaction kinetics than MnS and MnO. However, using MnSe as an anode material in SIBs can lead to serious volume change and lattice pulverization, which are common issues for TMSs and can result in poor cycling and rate performances. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref24 ref25 ref26 ref27" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref24 ref25 ref26 ref27" aria-label="reference 24 to 27">(24−27)</a> To address this challenge, a promising strategy is to integrate a carbon matrix with TMSs to increase electrical conductivity and tolerate structural expansion/shrinkage. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23 ref28 ref29 ref30" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref23 ref28 ref29 ref30" aria-label="reference 23 and 28 to 30">(23,28−30)</a> Designing a reasonable two-dimensional or yolk–shell structure can be an additional remedy, because it can increase the contact area with electrolyte, shorten the migration path of Na<sup>+</sup> and accelerate the reaction kinetics. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref31 ref32" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref31 ref32" aria-label="reference 31 and 32">(31,32)</a> Furthermore, the electrochemical reaction mechanism of MnSe has not been investigated yet. Therefore, a comprehensive study is necessary to unveil the charge storage mechanism, starting from the structure design.</p><p>Herein, we report the rational design and controlled preparation of  multicore–shell MnSe nanoparticle encapsulated N-doped carbon (MnSe@NC) nanorods as an advanced anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs). A template-engaged synthesis as well as further carbonization and selenization in Ar/H<sub>2</sub> atmosphere were employed to wrap MnSe nanoparticles within a N-doped carbon layer (as detailed in the <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/suppl_file/nl4c01408_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Experimental Section (Supporting Information)</a>). By design of a quasi-1D structure, the migration pathway of Na<sup>+</sup> ions was efficiently shortened, which greatly improved the rate performance. In addition, the N-doped carbon layer increased the conductivity and alleviated the volume variation and lattice collapse during cycling. The MnSe@NC anode exhibited remarkable rate performance (152.7 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 5 A g<sup>–1</sup>) and long cycle life (132.7 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> after 2000 cycles at 5 A g<sup>–1</sup>), which highlighted the great superiority of optimizing the microstructure to obtain advanced anode materials for SIBs. Importantly, the sodium intercalation behavior of the single-crystal MnSe film was <i>in situ</i> probed by transmission electron microscopy, allowing for monitoring reversible phase transformation of MnSe during the discharging process. Through a series of <i>in situ</i> and <i>ex situ</i> spectroscopy and microscopy characterizations, the highly reversible conversion reaction mechanism of MnSe during cycling was revealed, underscoring the great potential of MnSe@NC for serving as anode materials in high-performance SIBs.</p><p>As illustrated in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>a, a coordination polymer based on Mn<sup>2+</sup> and nitrilotriacetic acid (NTA) with a 3D framework of nanorods (namely, Mn-NTA) was synthesized as the precursor through a hydrothermal reaction. Next, the Mn precursor (Mn-NTA) and Se powders were annealed in a tube furnace under an Ar/H<sub>2</sub> atmosphere to form a multicore–shell structure (MnSe@NC), where MnSe particles were wrapped with a N-doped carbon layer. Detailed morphological and structural characteristics of the samples were observed using scanning electron microscopy (SEM) and transmission electron microscopy (TEM). <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/suppl_file/nl4c01408_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S1a,b</a> shows that the Mn-NTA precursor was uniform nanowires with the length ranging from 20 to 50 μm. Compared to the blocky structure of commercial MnSe powders in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/suppl_file/nl4c01408_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S2</a>, the SEM and TEM images (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>b–d) demonstrate that after annealing, the Mn-NTA template transformed into a multicore–shell morphology (MnSe@NC). The MnSe nanoparticles were encapsulated within an N-doped carbon shell with a thickness of approximately 5 nm, as depicted in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>d. The as-prepared quasi-1D nanostructure reduces the migration distance for electrons and Na<sup>+</sup> ions, which is helpful to boost reaction kinetics. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref24 ref33" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref24 ref33" aria-label="reference 24 and 33">(24,33)</a> Moreover, the N-doped carbon not only enhances the efficiency of electron transport and provides more active sites for Na<sup>+</sup> storage, but also mitigates the structural collapse caused by volume change during long-term cycling processes. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref34 ref35" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref34 ref35" aria-label="reference 34 and 35">(34,35)</a></p><figure id="fig1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/asset/images/medium/nl4c01408_0001.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/asset/images/large/nl4c01408_0001.jpeg" id="gr1" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 1. (a) Schematic illustration of the synthetic procedure of MnSe@NC. (b) SEM, (c–d) TEM, and (e) HRTEM images of MnSe@NC. (f–g) HAADF-STEM image and corresponding element mappings of MnSe@NC. (h) XRD spectra of MnSe@NC and commercial MnSe powders. (i–j) XPS spectra at (i) Mn 2pand (j) Se 3d regions of MnSe@NC and commercial MnSe powders.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/asset/images/large/nl4c01408_0001.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408&amp;id=fig1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p>To investigate the structural information on MnSe@NC, the HRTEM image (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>e) reveals an interplanar spacing of 0.274 nm, corresponding to the (220) crystal plane of α-MnSe. Energy dispersive X-ray spectroscopy (EDS) and high-angle annular dark field scanning TEM (HAADF-STEM) were performed to investigate the existence and distribution for elements. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>f,g directly reflect the uniform distribution of Mn, Se, N and C elements, indicating successful construction of the as-proposed multicore–shell structure. The introduction of nitrogen species into MnSe@NC nanorods could contribute to increasing the active sites of Na<sup>+</sup> storage and electrical conductivity. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref35 ref36 ref37" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref35 ref36 ref37" aria-label="reference 35 to 37">(35−37)</a> As a control, <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/suppl_file/nl4c01408_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S3 and S4</a> also demonstrated the existence of Mn and Se elements in the commercial MnSe.</p><p>The crystalline structures of MnSe@NC and commercial MnSe powders were measured via X-ray diffraction (XRD). The diffraction peaks (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>h) were verified to be cubic MnSe (JPCDS. no. 11–0683, α-MnSe). Thermogravimetric analysis (TGA) was applied to calculate the weight percentage of MnSe in MnSe@NC (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/suppl_file/nl4c01408_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S5</a>). The mass percentages of MnSe and N-doped carbon were calculated to be 61.27% and 38.73%, respectively. The N<sub>2</sub> adsorption–desorption curves, as well as the Brunauer–Emmett–Teller (BET) method, was employed to measure the pore diameter distribution of the samples (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/suppl_file/nl4c01408_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S6</a>). Compared with the low specific surface area of commercial MnSe powders (<i>S</i><sub>BET</sub> = 0.0059 m<sup>2</sup> g<sup>–1</sup>) (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/suppl_file/nl4c01408_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S6a</a>), the MnSe@NC possesses much larger specific surface area (<i>S</i><sub>BET</sub> = 34.82 m<sup>2</sup> g<sup>–1</sup>) with a pore size of 3.57 nm (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/suppl_file/nl4c01408_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S6b,c</a>), which contributes to the improved interface contact between electrolyte and active materials and the introduction of more active sites for Na<sup>+</sup> storage. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref38 ref39" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref38 ref39" aria-label="reference 38 and 39">(38,39)</a></p><p>X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) was employed to investigate the valence states and elemental compositions of the samples. Compared with the Mn 2p and Se 3d bands of commercial MnSe powders, the XPS survey of MnSe@NC in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/suppl_file/nl4c01408_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S7a</a> displays the characteristic peaks of Mn 2p, N 1s, C 1s and Se 3d. The high-resolution Mn 2p spectrum (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>i) shows double peaks at 652.9 and 641.3 eV, which are ascribed to Mn 2p<sub>1/2</sub> and Mn 2p<sub>3/2</sub>, while the peaks of commercial Se powders are at 653.1 (Mn 2p<sub>1/2</sub>) and 641.5 eV. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref29" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref29" aria-label="reference 29">(29)</a> The C 1s spectrum (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/suppl_file/nl4c01408_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S7b</a>) exhibits three peaks centered at 288.9 (C═O), 286.2 (C–N) and 284.8 eV (C–C). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref40" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref40" aria-label="reference 40">(40)</a> The N 1s spectrum (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/suppl_file/nl4c01408_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S7c</a>) shows a peak centered at 399.4 eV, corresponding to pyrrolic N, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref41" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref41" aria-label="reference 41">(41)</a> which can enhance the electron and ion transportation. Three peaks at 54.8, 55.8, and 60.0 eV in the Se 3d spectrum of MnSe@NC (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>j) correspond to Se–O, Se 3d<sub>3/2</sub> and Se 3d<sub>5/2</sub> bonds, respectively. Compared with MnSe@NC, the Se 3d spectrum of commercial MnSe powders can be deconvoluted into two obvious peaks at 55.0 and 56.0 eV, corresponding to Se 3d<sub>3/2</sub> and Se 3d<sub>5/2</sub>, respectively. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref26 ref42 ref43" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref26 ref42 ref43" aria-label="reference 26, 42 and 43">(26,42,43)</a></p><p>The electrochemical properties of MnSc@NC were evaluated in half batteries. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>a displays the initial five cycles of cyclic voltammogram (CV) curves within a voltage range of 0.01–3.00 V at a scan rate of 0.2 mV s<sup>–1</sup>. There are three main cathodic peaks (2.07, 1.12, and 0.19 V) in the first cathodic scan, corresponding to the Na<sup>+</sup> intercalation, the conversion reaction of MnSe, and the formation of solid electrolyte interface (SEI), respectively. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref43" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref43" aria-label="reference 43">(43)</a> In the subsequent cathodic scan, two main cathode peaks (1.64 and 0.61 V) correspond to the Na<sup>+</sup> intercalation reaction to form Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>MnSe and the conversion reaction to form metallic Mn and Na<sub>2</sub>Se, respectively. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref21" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref21" aria-label="reference 21">(21)</a> In the initial anodic scan, three main anodic peaks (1.51, 1.86, and 2.04 V) represent the transformation reaction of Mn to MnSe. In the subsequent anodic scan, the main anodic peaks are 1.51 and 2.04 V. The peak shift is caused by the irreversible reactions in the process of intercalation and conversion reaction. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref29 ref32" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref29 ref32" aria-label="reference 29 and 32">(29,32)</a> From the second cycle, the CV curves present high reversibility, suggesting that MnSe@NC as the electrode material may present outstanding cycling stability. By stark contrast, the redox peaks in the CV curves of commercial MnSe powders alter continuously, suggesting the inferior reversibility (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/suppl_file/nl4c01408_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S8</a>).</p><figure id="fig2" data-index="2" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 2</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/asset/images/medium/nl4c01408_0002.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/asset/images/large/nl4c01408_0002.jpeg" id="gr2" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 2. (a) CV curves of MnSe@NC in a potential range of 0.01–3.00 V at 0.2 mV s<sup>–1</sup>. (b) EIS curves, (c) Cyclic performance at 0.5 A g<sup>–1</sup> and (d) rate capability of MnSe@NC and commercial MnSe powders. (e) Long cycle performance of MnSe@NC electrode at 5 A g<sup>–1</sup> after three-cycle activation at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/asset/images/large/nl4c01408_0002.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408&amp;id=fig2"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p><a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/suppl_file/nl4c01408_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S9a</a> shows galvanostatic charge–discharge (GCD) profiles at a current density of 0.5 A g<sup>–1</sup>. The initial charge and discharge capacities of MnSe@NC are 361.7 and 448.1 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>, respectively, with a Coulombic efficiency (CE) of 80.7%. In comparison to commercial MnSe powders (as depicted in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/suppl_file/nl4c01408_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S9b</a>), the MnSe@NC anode exhibit a higher specific capacity and initial CE. In <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>b, the electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) curves display a sloping line in the low-frequency region and a semicircle in the medium and high-frequency regions, which represent diffusion resistance and charge transfer resistance (<i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>), respectively. The <i>R</i><sub>s</sub> represents the contact resistance of the battery. Compared with commercial MnSe powders (<i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> = 44.3 Ω, <i>R</i><sub>s</sub> = 13.0 Ω), the MnSe@NC anode show lower <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> (21.2 Ω) and <i>R</i><sub>s</sub> (11.1 Ω) values, indicating promoted interfacial kinetics and ion transport.</p><p>As shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>c, the discharge capacity of MnSe@NC anode at 0.5 A g<sup>–1</sup> after 200 cycles maintained at 232.1 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> with the capacity retention of 86.8% (calculated from the second cycle), which was much higher than 121.0 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> of commercial MnSe powders. Besides, the MnSe@NC anode exhibits more outstanding discharge capacities of 268.9, 253.5, 229.3, 207.0, 184.4, and 152.7 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.1, 0.2, 0.5, 1, 2, and 5 A g<sup>–1</sup> (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>d and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/suppl_file/nl4c01408_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S10</a>), respectively, indicating a better rate performance. More importantly, after activating at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>, the capacity of MnSe@NC anode after 2000 cycles still kept at 132.7 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> with a capacity retention of 72.4% (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>e), suggesting that the design of multicore–shell structures significantly contribute to improving the specific capacity and cycling stability for SIBs.</p><p>To demonstrate the pseudocapacitance behavior of the MnSe@NC anode, CV curves were performed at different scanning rates, as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>a. The related peak current (<i>i</i>) and scanning rate (<i>v</i>) correspond to the following formula: <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref39" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref39" aria-label="reference 39">(39)</a></p><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq1"><div class="equation"><span class="MathJax_Preview" style="color: inherit;"><span class="MJXp-math MJXp-display" id="MJXp-Span-1"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-2"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-3"><span class="MJXp-mstyle" id="MJXp-Span-4"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-5">i</span></span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-6"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-7" style="margin-left: 0.333em; margin-right: 0.333em;">=</span><span class="MJXp-mstyle" id="MJXp-Span-8"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-9">a</span><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-10"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-11" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-12">v</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-13" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-14">b</span></span></span></span></span></span></span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processed"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0" style=""><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1"><span style="display: inline-block; vertical-align: 0em; width: 0.287em; display: inline-block; overflow: hidden;"></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-41" style="font-family: STIXGeneral-Regular;">log</span><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-42"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-43" style="font-family: STIXGeneral-Regular;">(</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-44" style="font-family: STIXGeneral-Italic;">𝑣</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-45" style="font-family: STIXGeneral-Regular;">)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span></div><script type="math/mml" id="MathJax-Element-2"><math display="block" indentalign="left"><mrow><mrow><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><mi>log</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>i</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mstyle></mrow></mrow><mrow><mo linebreak="nobreak">=</mo><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><mi>log</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>a</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mo>+</mo><mi>b</mi><mspace width=".25em"></mspace><mi>log</mi><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>v</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mstyle></mrow></math></script></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(2)</span></div></div><p></p><figure id="fig3" data-index="3" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 3</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/asset/images/medium/nl4c01408_0003.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/asset/images/large/nl4c01408_0003.jpeg" id="gr3" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 3. (a) CV curves of MnSe@NC anode at the different scans between 0.2 to 1 mV s<sup>–1</sup>. (b) Log (<i>i</i>) vs. log (<i>v</i>) plots at specific peak currents. (c) Pseudocapacitive contribution ratios (blue) at different sweep rates. (d) CV profiles at 0.2 mV s<sup>–1</sup> showing the pseudocapacitive contribution (blue).</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/asset/images/large/nl4c01408_0003.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408&amp;id=fig3"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p>In <a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq1" aria-label="formula 1">formula 1</a>–<a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq2" aria-label="2">2</a>, <i>a</i> and <i>b</i> are two different variables. <i>b</i> represents the slope of log(<i>v</i>) versus log(<i>i</i>). <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>b shows that <i>b</i> values are close to 1.0, indicating that the electrochemical reaction is mainly controlled by pseudocapacitance behavior. The pseudocapacitance and diffusion contributions can be further calculated by the following formula:</p><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq3"><div class="equation"><span class="MathJax_Preview" style="color: inherit;"><span class="MJXp-math MJXp-display" id="MJXp-Span-40"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-41"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-42"><span class="MJXp-mstyle" id="MJXp-Span-43"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-44">I</span></span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-45"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-46" style="margin-left: 0.333em; As depicted in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>c,d, the pseudocapacitance contribution ratio increases with the increase of scan rate and can reach  60.07% at 1.0 mV s<sup>–1</sup>, indicating a significant contribution of pseudocapacitance behavior to sodium storage. In order to calculate the diffusion coefficient of Na<sup>+</sup> (<i>D</i><sub>Na<sup>+</sup></sub>), the galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) was applied, as follows:</p><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq4"><div class="equation"><span class="MathJax_Preview" style="color: inherit;"><span class="MJXp-math MJXp-display" id="MJXp-Span-67"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-68"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-69"><span class="MJXp-mstyle" id="MJXp-Span-70"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-71">D</span></span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-72"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-73" style="margin-left: 0.333em; border-top: none; border-bottom: 1px solid; margin: 0.1em 0px;"></span></span><span><span class="MJXp-box"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-83"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-84">π</span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-85">τ</span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-86"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-87" style="margin-left: 0em; margin-right: 0em; vertical-align: -0.689em;"><span class="MJXp-right MJXp-scale4" style="font-size: 3.756em; margin-left: -0.17em;">(</span></span><span class="MJXp-mfrac" id="MJXp-Span-88" style="vertical-align: 0.25em;"><span class="MJXp-box"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-89"><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-90">Δ</span><span class="MJXp-msub" id="MJXp-Span-91"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-92" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-93">E</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-94" style="vertical-align: -0.4em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-95">s</span></span></span></span></span><span class="MJXp-box" style="margin-top: -0.9em;"><span class="MJXp-denom"><span><span class="MJXp-rule" style="height: 1em; border-top: none; border-bottom: 1px solid; margin: 0.1em 0px;"></span></span><span><span class="MJXp-box"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-96"><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-97">Δ</span><span class="MJXp-msub" id="MJXp-Span-98"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-99" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-100">E</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-101" style="vertical-align: -0.4em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-102">t</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-103" style="margin-left: 0em; margin-right: 0em; vertical-align: -0.689em;"><span class="MJXp-right MJXp-scale4" style="font-size: 3.756em; margin-left: -0.17em;">)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processed"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-4-Frame" tabindex="0" style=""><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-76"><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.98em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.372em; left: 0.685em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-93"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-94" style="font-size: 70.7%; width: 0.06em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.98em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(0.855em, 1001.76em, 1.253em, -999.997em);
