width: 0px; height: 1.082em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-98"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-99" style="vertical-align: -0.452em;"><span><span style="font-size: 111%; font-family: STIXSizeTwoSym;">(</span></span></span><span class="mfrac" id="MathJax-Span-100"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.935em; height: 0px; margin-right: 0.116em; margin-left: 0.116em;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.128em, 1001.82em, 4.321em, -999.997em); top: -4.656em; left: 50%; margin-left: -0.906em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-101"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-102" style="font-family: STIXGeneral-Regular;">Δ</span><span class="msub" id="MathJax-Span-103"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.082em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.185em, 1000.74em, 4.151em, -999.997em); top: -3.974em; left: 0em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-104"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-105" style="font-family: STIXGeneral-Italic;">𝐸<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.98em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.804em; left: 0.741em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-106"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-107" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: STIXGeneral-Italic;">𝑠</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.98em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.98em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.128em, 1001.71em, 4.321em, -999.997em); top: -3.293em; left: 50%; margin-left: -0.849em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-108"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-109" style="font-family: STIXGeneral-Regular;">Δ</span><span class="msub" id="MathJax-Span-110"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.026em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.185em, 1000.74em, 4.151em, -999.997em); top: -3.974em; left: 0em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-111"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-112" style="font-family: STIXGeneral-Italic;">𝐸<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.98em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.804em; left: 0.741em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-113"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-114" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: STIXGeneral-Italic;">𝑡</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.98em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.98em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(0.855em, 1001.93em, 1.253em, -999.997em); top: -1.304em; left: 0em;"><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: 0em; border-top: 1.3px solid; width: 1.935em; height: 0px;"></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 1.082em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-115" style="vertical-align: -0.452em;"><span><span style="font-size: 111%; font-family: STIXSizeTwoSym;">)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span></div><script type="math/mml" id="MathJax-Element-4"><math display="block" indentalign="left"><mrow><mrow><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><mi>D</mi></mstyle></mrow></mrow><mrow><mo linebreak="nobreak">=</mo><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><mfrac><mrow><mn>4</mn><msup><mrow><mi>L</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn></mrow></msup></mrow><mrow><mi>π</mi><mi>τ</mi></mrow></mfrac><mrow><mo stretchy="true">(</mo><mfrac><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi><msub><mrow><mi>E</mi></mrow><mrow><mi>s</mi></mrow></msub></mrow><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi><msub><mrow><mi>E</mi></mrow><mrow><mi>t</mi></mrow></msub></mrow></mfrac><mo stretchy="true">)</mo></mrow></mstyle></mrow></math></script></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(4)</span></div></div>where τ represents the relaxation time (s). Δ<i>E</i><sub><i>s</i></sub> stands for the variation of potential (V) via the current pulse, and Δ<i>E</i><sub><i>t</i></sub> is variation  of potential (V) during the charging process. <i>L</i> stands for the length in Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion routes (cm), namely, the thickness of the electrode material. As depicted in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/suppl_file/nl4c01408_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S11</a>, the calculated <i>D</i><sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup> ranges from 10<sup>–11</sup> to 10<sup>–9</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>–1</sup>, indicating that the MnSe@NC anode possesses high reaction kinetics during cycling processes.<p></p><p>We further elaborated on the working mechanism of the MnSe anode for SIBs. To investigate the structural evolution of MnSe@NC during discharging, we first prepared an <i>in situ</i> TEM device with focus ion beam (FIB), as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>a–h and detailed in the <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/suppl_file/nl4c01408_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Experimental Section (SI)</a>. As shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>a, <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>e and <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>f, the as-prepared single-crystal α-MnSe film electrode was projected along the [001] direction. The [020] and [200] interplanar spacings were measured to be 0.27 nm. A tungsten (W) needle was covered with metal sodium and used as the Na source (Na, <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>b), which allows Na<sup>+</sup> insertion into the α-MnSe film upon contact. The structural evolution was observed and recorded on an aberration corrected TEM (AC-TEM). After closing the circuit and discharging the MnSe film (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>c), a significant phase transition was observed at the reaction sites (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>h) compared to the non-reaction sites (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>g). This was attributed to a transformation from the [001] direction of α-MnSe to the [111] direction of β-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>MnSe. As shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>h, the [220] interplanar spacing was measured to be 0.23 nm, which is slightly broader than that of standard β-MnSe (0.21 nm), probably owing to the insertion of Na<sup>+</sup> ions.</p><figure id="fig4" data-index="4" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 4</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/asset/images/medium/nl4c01408_0004.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/asset/images/large/nl4c01408_0004.jpeg" id="gr4" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 4. (a–h) <i>In situ</i> TEM analysis of sodium intercalation behavior of single-crystal α-MnSe film. (a) TEM image of the α-MnSe film before testing. (b) TEM image of the α-MnSe film and Na metal before testing. (c) TEM image at the beginning of contact. (d) TEM image after the contact and the insertion of Na<sup>+</sup> ions. (e,f) HRTEM images of single-crystal α-MnSe film before testing at different magnifications. (g,h) HRTEM images of single-crystal α-MnSe film after the insertion of Na<sup>+</sup> ions corresponding to none reaction sites and reaction sites, respectively. (i–k) The charge–discharge curve during the first cycle and corresponding <i>in situ</i> Raman spectra of MnSe@NC at various charge/discharge states. (l) Schematic illustration of the charge storage mechanism of MnSe@NC.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/asset/images/large/nl4c01408_0004.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408&amp;id=fig4"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p>To further verify the phase transformation mechanism, we employed in situ Raman spectroscopy to monitor the structural changes of the MnSe@NC electrode. As shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>i–k, the pristine MnSe@NC electrode (Point 1) presented three peaks centered at 125, 236, and 476 cm<sup>–1</sup>, which were assigned to LA, LO, and optical two-magnon excitation mode of α-MnSe, respectively. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref44" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref44" aria-label="reference 44">(44)</a> When the electrode was discharged to 2.05 V (Point 2), two broad peaks at 255 and 507 cm<sup>–1</sup> appeared, which were ascribed to A<sub>1g</sub> mode of β-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>MnSe. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref45" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref45" aria-label="reference 45">(45)</a> Upon discharging to 1.70 V (Point 3), the peaks of α-MnSe vanished gradually, and the peaks of β-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>MnSe were enhanced. After discharging to 0.01 V (Point 4), only the peaks of β-MnSe were present, suggesting the full conversion of α-MnSe to β-MnSe. When the MnSe SIBs were charged to 1.60 V (Point 5), the peaks of α-MnSe reappeared and were further enhanced during charging up to 1.95 V (Point 6). After charging to 3.00 V, only the peaks of α-MnSe were present, indicating a reversible phase transition between α-MnSe and β-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>MnSe occurred during cycling processes. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref46" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref46" aria-label="reference 46">(46)</a> XRD analysis of a recycled MnSe@NC electrode provided further confirmation of the presence of β-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>MnSe during the discharge–charge processes (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/suppl_file/nl4c01408_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S12</a>).</p><p><i>Ex situ</i> XRD patterns were used to further verify the working mechanism of the MnSe@NC anode (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/suppl_file/nl4c01408_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S13</a>). When discharging to 0.30 V, the diffraction peak (about 32.5°) of MnSe vanishes gradually, and meanwhile, a new diffraction peak (Na<sub>2</sub>Se) appears at 37.3°. When fully discharged to 0.01 V, the diffraction peak of Na<sub>2</sub>Se still exists and meanwhile <i>ex situ</i> HRTEM confirms the formation of Na<sub>2</sub>Se and metallic Mn (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/suppl_file/nl4c01408_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S14a</a>). When charged to 3.00 V, the diffraction peak of Na<sub>2</sub>Se disappeared completely and, consequently, the diffraction peak of MnSe began to reappear. Additionally, <i>ex situ</i> HRTEM also indicated that MnSe regenerated (as shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/suppl_file/nl4c01408_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S14b</a>), thereby confirming the excellent structural reversibility of MnSe@NC.</p><p>Furthermore, <i>ex situ</i> XPS was utilized to monitor the changes in chemical valence states and the formation of the SEI film. When fully discharged to 0.01 V, Mn 2p (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/suppl_file/nl4c01408_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S15a</a>) and Se 3d (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/suppl_file/nl4c01408_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S15b</a>) peaks shift toward lower binding energies, suggesting the decrease in their chemical valence states, which then migrate to high binding energies at fully charged state (3.00 V). These changes are consistent with the structural evolution revealed by <i>in situ</i> studies, further confirming the highly reversible conversion reaction mechanism of MnSe@NC during charge/discharge processes. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref47" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref47" aria-label="reference 47">(47)</a> Meanwhile, <i>ex situ</i> XPS was applied to explore the surface compositions of the MnSe@NC electrode. At 0.01 and 3.00 V, there are four fitted peaks (C–C, C–O, C═O, and O─C═O) in C 1s spectra (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/suppl_file/nl4c01408_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S15c</a>), mainly originating from the components of SEI film, including Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> and sodium alkoxides, which provide a foundation for the stable operation of MnSe@NC. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref47 ref48" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref47 ref48" aria-label="reference 47 and 48">(47,48)</a> In the N 1s spectrum (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/suppl_file/nl4c01408_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S15d</a>), a slight change corresponding to pyrrolic N was observed, which is beneficial for enhancing the electrical conductivity of the carbon layer during cycling processes. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref49" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref49" aria-label="reference 49">(49)</a></p><p>Based on the above analysis, the sodium storage mechanism of MnSe@NC can be illustrated in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>l and described in the following formulas:</p><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq5"><div class="equation"><span class="MathJax_Preview" style="color: inherit;"><span class="MJXp-math MJXp-display" class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq7"><div class="equation"><span class="MathJax_Preview" style="color: inherit;"><span class="MJXp-math MJXp-display" id="MJXp-Span-154"><span class="MJXp-mrow" class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-170" style="margin-left: 0.267em; margin-right: 0.267em;">−</span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-171">x</span><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-172" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-176">a</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-177" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-178">+</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-179" style="margin-left: 0.267em; margin-right: 0.267em;">+</span><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-180"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-181" style="margin-left: 0em; margin-right: 0em;">(</span><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-182">4</span><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-183" style="margin-left: 0.267em; margin-right: 0.267em;">−</span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-184">x</span><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-185" style="margin-left: 0em; margin-right: 0em;">)</span></span><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-186"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-187" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-188">e</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-189" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-190">−</span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-191"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-192" style="margin-left: 0.333em; margin-right: 0.333em;">↔</span><span class="MJXp-mstyle" id="MJXp-Span-193"><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-194">Mn</span><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-195" style="margin-left: 0.267em; margin-right: 0.267em;">+</span><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-196">2</span><span class="MJXp-msub" id="MJXp-Span-197"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-198" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-199">Na</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-200" style="vertical-align: -0.4em;"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-201">2</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-202">Se</span></span></span></span></span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-7-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/mml" id="MathJax-Element-7"><math display="block" indentalign="left"><mrow><mrow><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><mi>β</mi><mo lspace="0" rspace="0">‐</mo><msub><mrow><mi>Na</mi></mrow><mrow><mi>x</mi></mrow></msub><mi>MnSe</mi><mo>+</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>4</mn><mo>−</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">N</mi><msup><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">a</mi></mrow><mrow><mo>+</mo></mrow></msup><mo>+</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>4</mn><mo>−</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><msup><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">e</mi></mrow><mrow><mo>−</mo></mrow></msup></mstyle></mrow></mrow><mrow><mo linebreak="nobreak">↔</mo><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><mi>Mn</mi><mo>+</mo><mn>2</mn><msub><mrow><mi>Na</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn></mrow></msub><mi>Se</mi></mstyle></mrow></math></script></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(7)</span></div></div><p></p><p>To investigate the potential of the MnSe@NC anode in practical applications, a SIB full cell was assembled with MnSe@NC as the anode and commercial Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> as the cathode (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>a). The Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> cathode in a SIB half cell can deliver a discharge capacity of ∼120 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup> for 300 cycles (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/suppl_file/nl4c01408_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S16</a>). The GCD profiles of the Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> half cell is depicted in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>b, where the two plateaus centering at approximately 3.32 and 3.15 V were assigned to the reduction reaction from V<sup>4+</sup> to V<sup>3+</sup>. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref50" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref50" aria-label="reference 50">(50)</a> The MnSe@NC||Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> SIB full cell exhibited a clear discharge voltage plateau in the range of 3.27–3.25 V and a slope between 3.00–2.70 V (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>c). The MnSe@NC||Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> SIB full cell can deliver a discharge capacity of 39.3 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> (corresponding to an energy density of 117.9 W h kg<sup>–1</sup>) at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup> (300 W kg<sup>–1</sup>) after 200 cycles (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>d). The energy density was calculated based on the mass of cathode materials. The relative high energy density (117.9 W h kg<sup>–1</sup>) and high discharge voltage (∼3.00 V) demonstrate that the design of the MnSe@NC||Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> SIB full cell is prospective in practical applications.</p><figure id="fig5" data-index="5" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 5</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/asset/images/medium/nl4c01408_0005.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/asset/images/large/nl4c01408_0005.jpeg" id="gr5" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 5. (a) Schematic diagram of the SIB full cell based on the MnSe@NC anode and Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> cathode. (b) GCD profiles of the Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> cathode at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>. (c) GCD profiles of the SIB full cell at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>. (d) Cycling performance of the SIB full cell at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408/asset/images/large/nl4c01408_0005.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acs.nanolett.4c01408&amp;id=fig5"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="last">To summarize, MnSe nanoparticles were successfully synthesized and encapsulated in an N-doped carbon layer to form multicore–shell structured MnSe@NC nanorods through a simple selenization process with Mn-NTA precursor. The structural evolution of MnSe@NC anode during charge/discharge processes was monitored using <i>in situ</i> AC-TEM and Raman spectra, confirming the high structural reversibility. <i>Ex situ</i> characterization techniques (XRD, XPS and HRTEM) further confirmed that the electrochemical mechanism of MnSe@NC nanorods was a highly reversible conversion reaction, accompanied by a reversible phase transition between α-MnSe and β-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>MnSe during cycling processes. Due to the unique quasi-1D multicore–shell structure and highly reversible conversion reaction mechanism, the MnSe@NC anode material demonstrated excellent rate performance (152.7 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at5 A g<sup>–1</sup>) and prolonged cycle life (132.7 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> after 2000 cycles at 5 A g<sup>–1</sup>) for sodium-ion batteries. This study highlights the importance of reasonable structural design of metal selenide based anode materials in improving sodium storage capability and reversibility and provides insights for the construction of high-specific-energy and long cycling SIBs.</p><div class="NLM_back"><div class="article_supporting-info" id="notes-4"><div class="article_content-header"><div                         cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">FeSe2@C Microrods as a Superior Long-Life and High-Rate Anode for Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pan, Qichang; Zhang, Man; Zhang, Lixuan; Li, Yahao; Li, Yu; Tan, Chunlei; Zheng, Fenghua; Huang, Youguo; Wang, Hongqiang; Li, Qingyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition-metal selenides have emerged as promising anode materials for sodium ion batteries (SIBs).  Nevertheless, they suffer from vol. expansion, polyselenide dissoln., and sluggish kinetics, which lead to inadequate conversion reaction toward sodium and poor reversibility during the desodiation process.  Therefore, the transition-metal selenides are far from long cycling stability, outstanding rate performance, and high initial Coulombic efficiency, which are the major challenges for practical application in SIBs.  Here, an efficient anode material including an FeSe2 core and N-doped carbon shell with inner void space as well as high cond. is developed for outstanding rate performance and long cycle life SIBs.  In the ingeniously designed FeSe2@NC microrods, the N-doped carbon shell can facilitate mass transport/electron transfer, protect the FeSe2 core from the electrolyte, and accommodate vol. variation of FeSe2 with the help of the inner void of the core.  Thus, the FeSe2@NC microrods can maintain strong structural integrity upon long cycling and ensure a good reversible conversion reaction of FeSe2 during the discharge/charge process.  As a result, the as-prepd. FeSe2@NC microrods exhibit excellent sodium storage performance and ultrahigh stability, achieving an excellent rate capability (411 mAh g-1 at 10.0 A g-1) and a long-term cycle performance (401.3 mAh g-1 after 2000 cycles at 5.0 A g-1).</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref2" class="refNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit2" data-doi="10.1002/anie.202004914"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zeng, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Enhanced multiple anchoring and catalytic conversion of polysulfides by amorphous MoS<sub>3</sub> nanoboxes for high-performance Li-S batteries</span>. <i>Angew.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The practical implementation of lithium-sulfur batteries is obstructed by poor cond., sluggish redox kinetics, the shuttle effect, large vol. variation, and low areal loading of sulfur electrodes.  Now, amorphous N-doped carbon/MoS3 (NC/MoS3) nanoboxes with hollow porous architectures have been meticulously designed as an advanced sulfur host.  Benefiting from the enhanced cond. by the N-doped carbon, reduced shuttle effect by the strong chem. interaction between unsatd. Mo and lithium polysulfides, improved redox reaction kinetics by the catalytic effect of MoS3, great tolerance of vol. variation and high sulfur loading arising from flexible amorphous materials with hollow-porous structures, the amorphous NC/MoS3 nanoboxes enabled sulfur electrodes to deliver a high areal capacity with superior rate capacity and decent cycling stability.                         cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium transition metal oxides: the preferred cathode choice for future sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Qiannan; Hu, Zhe; Li, Weijie; Zou, Chao; Jin, Huile; Wang, Shun; Chou, Shulei; Dou, Shi-Xue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The exploration of next-generation sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) is a worldwide concern to replace the current com. lithium-ion batteries, mitigating the increasing exhaustion of Li resources.  Sodium transition metal oxides are considered to be one of the most promising cathode materials for SIBs.  The anionic redox reaction in Li-rich transition metal oxides is capable of providing extra capacity in addn. to the cationic redox activities in lithium-ion batteries.  A similar phenomenon exists in SIBs, which even applies to Na-deficient transition metal oxides.  Moreover, transition metal oxides with mixed phase also demonstrate great potential.  In this review, studies on anionic redox are first systematically introduced.  The up-to-date advances on high-capacity transition metal oxide cathode materials for SIBs are then classified and summarized in different groups assocd. with or without anionic redox.  The existing challenges as well as available solns. and strategies are discussed, and proposals with new insights are made at the end.  It is expected that this work can provide new perspectives on controlling the anionic redox activity and finding novel high-capacity oxide cathode materials for SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref4" class="refNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit4" data-doi="10.1021/acs.nanolett.8b05189"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xue, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ren, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Rayleigh-instability-induced bismuth nanorod@nitrogen-doped carbon nanotubes as a long cycling and high rate anode for sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Nano Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>19</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1998</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">2004</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

However, the development of SIBs is limited by the lacking of proper anodes with long cycling life-spans and large reversible capacities.  Here the authors present rational synthesis of Rayleigh instability-induced Bi nanorods encapsulated in N-doped C nanotubes (Bi@N-C) using Bi2S3 nanobelts as the template for high-performance SIB.  The Bi@N-C electrode delivers superior Na storage performance in half cells, including a high specific capacity (410 mA h g-1 at 50 mA g-1), long cycling lifespan (1000 cycles), and superior rate capability (368 mA h g-1 at 2 A g-1).             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Constructing a heterojunction and introducing an interfacial interaction by designing ideal structures have the inherent advantages of optimizing electronic structures and macroscopic mech. properties.  An exquisite hierarchical heterogeneous structure of bimetal sulfide Sb2S3@FeS2 hollow nanorods embedded into a nitrogen-doped carbon matrix is fabricated by a concise two-step solvothermal method.  The FeS2 interlayer expands in situ grow on the interface of hollow Sb2S3 nanorods within the nitrogen-doped graphene matrix, forming a delicate heterostructure.  Such a well-designed architecture affords rapid Na+ diffusion and improves charge transfer at the heterointerfaces.  Meanwhile, the strongly synergistic coupling interaction among the interior Sb2S3, interlayer FeS2, and external nitrogen-doped carbon matrix creates a stable nanostructure, which extremely accelerates the electronic/ion transport and effectively alleviates the vol. expansion upon long cyclic performance.  As a result, the composite, as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries, exhibits a superior rate capability of 537.9 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1 and excellent cyclic stability with 85.7% capacity retention after 1000 cycles at 5 A g-1.  Based on the DFT calcn., the existing constructing heterojunction in this composite can not only optimize the electronic structure to enhance the cond. but also favor the Na2S adsorption energy to accelerate the reaction kinetics.  The outstanding electrochem. performance sheds light on the strategy by the rational design of hierarchical heterogeneous nanostructures for energy storage applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref7" class="refNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit7" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.1c05590"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Y.                 10.1021/acsaem.1c00967</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D4%26publication_year%3D2021%26pages%3D6874-6882%26journal%3DACS%2BAppl.%2BEnergy%2BMater.%26author%3DX.%2BJiang%26author%3DT.%2BCao%26author%3DF.%2BZhang%26author%3DJ.%2BZhang%26author%3DK.%2BQin%26author%3DH.%2BLiu%26author%3DY.%2BXia%26title%3DNitrogen-doped%2Bporous%2Bcarbon%2Bframework%2Bsupports%2Bultrafine%2BFeS2%2Bnanoparticles%2Bas%2Badvanced%2Bperformance%2Banode%2Bmaterials%2Bfor%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsaem.1c00967&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.4c01408&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsaem.1c00967&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen-Doped Porous Carbon Framework Supports Ultrafine FeS2 Nanoparticles as Advanced Performance Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jiang, Xiuyong; Cao, Tong; Zhang, Fan; Zhang, Jianhua; Qin, Kai; Liu, Haimei; Xia, Yongyao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6874-6882</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAEMCQ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2574-0962</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">FeS2 as a sodium-ion battery anode material has attracted great attention on account of its high theor. capacity, abundance, low cost, and other advantages.  However, the poor elec. cond. of FeS2 and the huge vol. expansion in the sodium-ion insertion/extn. process are the key factors affecting its electrochem. performance.  Herein, NaCl was used as a template to successfully synthesize a composite material of a nitrogen-doped porous carbon framework loaded with ultrafine FeS2 nanoparticles (FeS2/NPCF).  The three-dimensional porous carbon framework improves the cond. of the material as well as effectively suppresses the vol. expansion of the material during the charge and discharge process, thus improving the cycle performance of the composite material.  In the three-dimensional porous carbon framework with a larger sp. surface area, ultrafine FeS2 particles can lessen the diffusion distance and enhance the Na+ diffusion rate.  The ultrafine FeS2 nanoparticles loaded on the nitrogen-doped highly conductive porous carbon framework reduce the e-transport resistance and limit the vol. change of FeS2 during the cycle, which improves the structure's stability.  These advantages make FeS2/NPCF an ideal anode electrode material of a sodium-ion battery that shows excellent sodium storage performance.  A reversible capacity of 552 mAh g-1 is maintained with a capacity retention of 87% at 0.5A g-1 after 100 cycles.  Remarkably, even at 5A g-1, the FeS2/NPCF electrode still delivers a discharge capacity of 430 mAh g-1after 500 cycles.  FeS2/NPCF, with its excellent electrochem. performance, is considered a potential anode material for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref9" class="refNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit9" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201807753"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mohrhusen, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ali, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chung, K.                         cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchically Designed Nitrogen-Doped MoS2/Silicon Oxycarbide Nanoscale Heterostructure as High-Performance Sodium-Ion Battery Anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lim, Hyojun; Yu, Seungho; Choi, Wonchang; Kim, Sang-Ok</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">15</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7409-7420</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Molybedenum disulfide (MoS2) is regarded as a promising anode material for next-generation sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) owing to its high theor. capacity.  However, its low cond., large vol. changes, and undesirable phase transformation hinder its practical applications.  In this study, we synthesize a hierarchically designed core-shell heterostructure based on nitrogen-doped MoS2/C and silicon oxycarbide (SiOC) (N-MoS2/C@SiOC) via the facile pyrolysis of a suspension of an N-MoS2/polyfurfural precursor in silicone oil.  The in situ nitrogen doping in a two-dimensional MoS2 structure with carbon incorporation leads to the enlargement of the interlayer spacing and enhancement of the electronic cond. and mech. stability, which allows the facile, highly reversible insertion and extn. of sodium ions upon cycling.  Further, the nanoscale SiOC shell with surface capacitive reactivity provides a conductive pathway, preventing unfavorable side reactions at the electrode/electrolyte interface and acting as a structure-reinforcing buffer against severe vol. expansion issues.  As a result, the N-MoS2/C@SiOC composite exhibits high reversible capacity (540.7 mAh g-1), high-capacity retention (&gt;100% after 200 cycles), and excellent rate capability up to 10 A g-1.  The simple hierarchical core-shell design strategy developed in this study allows for the fabrication of high-performance metal sulfide anodes as well as other high-capacity anode materials for energy storage applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref12" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201706317"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, D.                         cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ion reservoir enabled by hierarchical bimetallic sulfides nanocages toward highly effective sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yuan, Jin; Qu, Baihua; Zhang, Qingfei; He, Wei; Xie, Qingshui; Peng, Dong-Liang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Designing and constructing bimetallic hierarchical structures is vital for the conversion-alloy reaction anode of sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Particularly, the rationally designed hetero-interface engineering can offer fast diffusion kinetics in the interface, leading to the improved high-power surface pseudocapacitance and cycling stability for SIBs.  Herein, the hierarchical zinc-tin sulfide nanocages (ZnS-NC/SnS2) are constructed through hydrothermal and sulfuration reactions.  The unconventional hierarchical design with internal void space greatly optimizes the structure stability, and bimetallic sulfide brings a bimetallic composite interface and N heteroatom doping, which are devoted to high electrochem. activity and improved interfacial charge transfer rate for Na+ storage.  Remarkably, the ZnS-NC/SnS2 composite anode exhibits a delightful reversible capacity of 595 mAh g-1 after 100 cycles at 0.2 A g-1, and long cycling capability for 500 cycles with a low capacity loss of 0.08% per cycle at 1 A g-1.  This study opens up a new route for rationally constructing hierarchical heterogeneous interfaces and sheds new light on efficient anode material for SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref14" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202303211"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sari, H.                 10.1007/s41918-022-00174-2</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D6%26publication_year%3D2023%26pages%3D5%26journal%3DElectrochem.%2BEnergy%2BRev.%26issue%3D1%26author%3DT.%2BBashir%26author%3DS.%2BZhou%26author%3DS.%2BYang%26author%3DS.%2BIsmail%26author%3DT.%2BAli%26author%3DH.%2BWang%26author%3DJ.%2BZhao%26author%3DL.%2BGao%26title%3DProgress%2Bin%2B3D-MXene%2BElectrodes%2Bfor%2BLithium%252FSodium%252FPotassium%252FMagnesium%252FZinc%252FAluminum-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1007%252Fs41918-022-00174-2&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.4c01408&amp;doiOfLink=10.1007%2Fs41918-022-00174-2&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Progress in 3D-MXene Electrodes for Lithium/Sodium/Potassium/Magnesium/Zinc/Aluminum-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Bashir, Tariq; Zhou, Shaowen; Yang, Shiqi; Ismail, Sara Adeeba; Ali, Tariq; Wang, Hao; Zhao, Jianqing; Gao, Lijun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochemical Energy Reviews</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EERLAM</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2520-8136</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer International Publishing AG</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Abstr.: MXenes have attracted increasing attention because of their rich surface functional groups, high elec. cond., and outstanding dispersibility in many solvents, and have demonstrated competitive efficiency in energy storage and conversion applications.  However, the restacking nature of MXene nanosheets like other two-dimensional (2D) materials through van der Waals forces results in sluggish ionic kinetics, restricted no. of active sites, and ultimate deterioration of MXene material/device performance.  The strategy of raising 2D MXenes into three-dimensional (3D) structures has been considered an efficient way for reducing restacking, providing greater porosity, higher surface area, and shorter distances for mass transport of ions, surpassing std. one-dimensional (1D) and 2D structures.  In multivalent ion batteries, the pos. multivalent ions combine with two or more electrons at the same time, so their capacities are two or three times that of lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) under the same conditions, e.g., a magnesium ion battery has a high theor. specific capacity of 2 205 mAh g-1 and a high volumetric capacity of 3 833 mAh cm-3.  In this review, we summarize the most recent strategies for fabricating 3D MXene architectures, such as assembly, template, 3D printing, electrospinning, aerogel, and gas foaming methods.  Special consideration has been given to the applications of highly porous 3D MXenes in energy storage devices beyond LIBs, such as sodium ion batteries (SIBs), potassium ion batteries (KIBs), magnesium ion batteries (MIBs), zinc ion batteries (ZIBs), and aluminum ion batteries (AIBs).  Finally, the authors provide a summary of the future opportunities and challenges for the construction of 3D MXenes and MXene-based electrodes for applications beyond LIBs.  Graphic Abstr.: [graphic not available: see fulltext].</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref18" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1021/acs.nanolett.1c01595"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Johnson, I.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kudo, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Effect of local atomic structure on sodium ion storage in hard amorphous carbon</span>. <i>Nano Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>21</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">6504</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">6510</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acs.nanolett.1c01595</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D21%26publication_year%3D2021%26pages%3D6504-6510%26journal%3DNano%2BLett.%26author%3DJ.%2BHan%26author%3DI.%2BJohnson%26author%3DZ.%2BLu%26author%3DA.%2BKudo%26author%3DM.%2BChen%26title%3DEffect%2Bof%2Blocal%2Batomic%2Bstructure%2Bon%2Bsodium%2Bion%2Bstorage%2Bin%2Bhard%2Bamorphous%2Bcarbon%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facs.nanolett.1c01595&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.4c01408&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.1c01595&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Effect of Local Atomic Structure on Sodium Ion Storage in Hard Amorphous Carbon</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Han, Jiuhui; Johnson, Isaac; Lu, Zhen; Kudo, Akira; Chen, Mingwei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">21</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">15</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6504-6510</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The fundamental understanding of sodium storage mechanisms in amorphous carbon is essential to develop high-performance anode materials for sodium-ion batteries.  However, the intrinsic relation between the structure of amorphous carbon and Na+ storage remains to be debated due to the difficulty in controlling and characterizing the local at. configurations of amorphous carbon.  Here we report quant. measurements of Na+ storage in a low-temp. dealloyed hard carbon with a tunable local structure from completely disordered micropores to gradually increased graphitic order domains.  The structure-capacity-potential correlation not only verifies the disputing "adsorption-intercalation" mechanisms, i.e., Na+ intercalation into local graphitic domains for the low-voltage plateaus and adsorption in fully disordered carbon for the sloping voltage profiles, but also unveils a new mechanism of Na+ adsorption on defective sites of graphitic carbon in the medium-potential sloping region.  The quant. investigations provide essential insights into the reaction mechanisms of Na+ with amorphous carbon for designing advanced sodium-ion battery anodes.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref19" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202003911"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lai, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ultrahigh phosphorus doping of carbon for high-rate sodium ion batteries anode</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrahigh Phosphorus Doping of Carbon for High-Rate Sodium Ion Batteries Anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yan, Jie; Li, Haomiao; Wang, Kangli; Jin, Qianzheng; Lai, Chenglong; Wang, Ruxing; Cao, Shengling; Han, Jing; Zhang, Zhuchan; Su, Jinzhao; Jiang, Kai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">21</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2003911</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADEMBC</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Phosphorus doped carbons are of particular interest as anode materials because of their large interlayer spacing and strong adsorption of Na+ ions.  However, it remains challenging to achieve high phosphorus doping due to the limited choices of phosphorus sources and the difficulty in constructing oxygen-free synthesis system.  Herein, a new synthesis strategy is proposed to prep. ultrahigh phosphorus-doped carbon (UPC) anodes for high performance sodium ion batteries (SIBs).  By using two commonly available, miscible, evaporable liqs. in PCl3 and C6H12, as phosphorus and carbon sources, an oxygen-free reaction system is successfully established by N2 bubbling to simultaneously realize carbonization and in situ P doping.  The P content can reach 30 wt%, much higher than most reported P-doping carbon-based materials.  Furthermore, the doped P is dominated by substitutional P-(C3) protrusions in the carbon lattice, which can significantly enlarge the interlayer spacing and enhance the adsorption energy of Na+.  When serving as the SIBs anode, the UPC delivers an ultrahigh reversible capacity of 510.4 mAh g-1 with a rational operating voltage of 0.54 V, and the best rate capability of 397.1 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1.  This new strategy will effectively promote the practical application of hard carbon.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref20" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201606023"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Noonan, O.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Tailored yolk-shell Sn@C nanoboxes for high-performance lithium storage</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Microsized Gray Tin as a High-Rate and Long-Life Anode Material for Advanced Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Yansong; Yao, Qian; Shao, Ruiwen; Wang, Cheng; Yan, Weishan; Ma, Jizhen; Liu, Duo; Yang, Jian; Qian, Yitai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are developed to address the serious concern about the limited resources of lithium.  To achieve high energy d., anode materials with a large specific capacity and a low operation voltage are highly desirable.  Herein, microsized particles of gray Sn (α-Sn) are explored as an anode material of SIBs for the first time.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical porous Co0.85Se@reduced graphene oxide ultrathin nanosheets with vacancy-enhanced kinetics as superior anodes for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Yongxin; Wang, Ziheng; Jiang, Ying; Li, Shuaijie; Li, Zehua; Zhang, Haiqin; Wu, Feng; Xie, Man; Li, Li; Chen, Renjie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metal selenides have received much attention from the rechargeable battery community owing to their considerable capacity.  However, attainment of a long cycle life and fast Na+ storage kinetics are still needed to enable their practical application.  Co0.85Se nanosheets prepd. using a simple hydrothermal method exhibit a hierarchical porous structure, which is conducive to fast electrolyte transport and rapid adsorption of Na+ ions.  Herein, to improve the electronic cond. of Co0.85Se, reduced graphene oxide (rGO) is introduced to construct a three-dimensional network and achieve fast electronic transport.  This defect-controlled Co0.85Se@rGO anode exhibits a highly reversible capacity of 460 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 0.5 A g-1.  Outstanding durability and remarkable rate stability are also achieved via the synergistic effects of vacancy transport and the heterostructure between Co0.85Se and rGO.  Furthermore, the Na+ insertion/extn. mechanism is systematically investigated using ex situ X-ray diffraction, Raman spectroscopy, high-resoln. transmission electron microscopy, and a series of electrochem. analyses.  These analyses enable detailed characterization of the ionic diffusion kinetics and corresponding components and structural changes.  Finally, a first-principles approach is employed to det. the diffusion energy barrier of Na+ ions in perfect CoSe and defective Co0.85Se.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref24" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1002/smll.202004580"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Willow-leaf-like ZnSe@N-doped carbon nanoarchitecture as a stable and high-performance anode material for sodium-ion and potassium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>16</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">2004580</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Willow-Leaf-Like ZnSe@N-Doped Carbon Nanoarchitecture as a Stable and High-Performance Anode Material for Sodium-Ion and Potassium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dong, Caifu; Wu, Leqiang; He, Yanyan; Zhou, Yanli; Sun, Xiuping; Du, Wei; Sun, Xueqin; Xu, Liqiang; Jiang, Fuyi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">16</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">47</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">ZnSe is regarded as a promising anode material for energy storage due to its high theor. capacity and environment friendliness.  Nevertheless, it is still a significant challenge to obtain superior electrode materials with stable performance owing to the serious vol. change and aggregation upon cycling.  Herein, a willow-leaf-like N-doped C-coated ZnSe (ZnSe@NC) composite synthesized through facile solvothermal and subsequent selenization process is beneficial to expose more active sites and facilitate the fast electron/ion transmission.  These merits significantly enhance the electrochem. performances of ZnSe@NC for Na-ion batteries (SIBs) and K-ion batteries (PIBs).  The obtained ZnSe@NC exhibits outstanding rate performance (440.3 mA-h g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 and 144.4 mA-h g-1 at 10 A g-1) and ultralong cycle stability (242.2 mA-h g-1 at 8.0 A g-1 even after 3200 cycles) for SIBs. and 106.5 mA-h g-1 can be retained after 550 cycles and 71.4 mA-h g-1 is still remained after 1500 cycles at 200 mA g-1 when applied as anode for PIBs, indicating good cycle stability of the electrode.  The possible electrochem. mechanism and the ionic diffusion kinetics of the ZnSe@NC are studied using ex situ x-ray diffraction, high-resoln.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Coaxial nanotubes are a significant class of nanoscale building blocks for advanced electrodes of secondary batteries.  Herein, one-dimensional (1D) coaxial double nanotubes (DNTs) consisting of α-MnSe inner tubes and N-doped carbon (N-C) outer tubes (abbreviated as α-MnSe@N-C DNTs) are successfully prepd. and are demonstrated to be promising anode material for Li-ion and Na-ion batteries (LIBs/NIBs).  When used in LIBs, it was revealed by ex situ XRD/HRTEM studies and electrode kinetics that a new electrochem. α → β phase transition plays a crucial role in improving the cycling stability.  As a result, the α-MnSe@N-C DNTs electrode delivers a high Li-storage capacity (800 mA h g-1 at 50 mA g-1), excellent rate capability (405 mA h g-1 at 14 A g-1) and ultra-long cycling stability (a high capacity retention of 87.2% even after 9000 cycles at 2 A g-1) with retained 1D morphol.  In addn., the outer N-C nanotube can effectively protect the active α-MnSe inner nanotube to realize such outstanding electrochem. properties owing to the high elec. cond. and particular 1D coaxial nanoarchitecture of the inner nanotube.  Moreover, α-MnSe@N-C DNTs also exhibit excellent Li/Na-storage properties and full-cell performances when coupled with com. LiFePO4 and LiNi0.6Co0.2Mn0.2O2 cathodes in LIBs as well as with the Na3V2(PO4)2O2F cathode in NIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref26" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1088/1361-6528/ab8e78"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">MnSe embedded in carbon nanofibers as advanced anode material for sodium ion batteries</span>. <i>Nanotechnology</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>31</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">335402</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">MnSe with high theor. capacity and reversibility is considered as a promising material for the anode of sodium ion batteries.  In this study, MnSe nanoparticles embedded in 1D carbon nanofibers (MnSe-NC) are successfully prepd. via facile electrospinning and subsequent selenization.  A carbon framework can effectively protect MnSe dispersed in it from agglomeration and can accommodate vol. variation in the conversion reaction between MnSe and Na+ to guarantee cycling stability.  The 1D fiber structure can increase the area of contact between electrode and electrolyte to shorten the diffusion path of Na+ and facilitate its transfer.  According to the kinetic anal., the storage process of sodium by MnSe-NC is a surface pseudocapacitive-controlled process with promising rate capability.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Bilateral Interfaces in In2Se3-CoIn2-CoSe2 Heterostructures for High-Rate Reversible Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiao, Shuhao; Li, Xinyan; Zhang, Wensi; Xiang, Yong; Li, Tingshuai; Niu, Xiaobin; Chen, Jun Song; Yan, Qingyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

Herein, we fabricated In2Se3/CoSe2 hollow nanorods composed of In2Se3/ CoIn2/ CoSe2 by growing cobalt-based zeolitic imidazolate framework ZIF-67 on the surface of indium-based metal-org. framework MIL-68, followed by in situ gaseous selenization.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Two-phase or multiphase compds. have been evidenced to exhibit good electrochem. performance for energy applications; however, the mechanism insights into these materials, esp. the performance improvement by engineering the high-active phase boundaries in bimetallic compds., remain to be seen.  Here, we report a bimetallic selenide heterostructure (CoSe2/ZnSe) and the fundamental mechanism behind their superior electrochem. performance.  The charge redistribution at the phase boundaries of CoSe2/ZnSe was exptl. and theor. proven.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Facile synthesis of Manganese selenide anchored in Three-Dimensional carbon nanosheet matrix with enhanced Lithium storage properties</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu, Litao; Zhang, Liguo; Kang, Jun; Kim, Kwang Ho</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Manganese selenide (MnSe), a conversion-type anode for Lithium-ion batteries with low cost and high specific capacity, is impeded the development by drastic vol. changes and poor kinetics in Li+ insertion/desertion processes.  In this study, we successfully synthesized uniform MnSe nanoparticles anchored in 3D carbon nanosheet matrix (MnSe ⊂ 3DCNM) via a facile sol-gel and selenation route.  The obtained 3DCNM contributes high surface area, increased active sites for N-doping, excellent elec. cond. and stable nanostructure to MnSe ⊂ 3DCNM, thereby leading to full lithiation/delithiation reactions, excellent electrochem. kinetics and buffer vol. expansion of MnSe nanoparticles. When combined with LiMn2O4 cathode, the MnSe ⊂ 3DCNM-1.92//LiMn2O4 full cells also exhibit excellent electrochem. properties.  The kinetic anal. and EIS results demonstrate the generation of intermediate LixMnSe phase and the irreversible phase transformation of α-MnSe → β-MnSe with decreased diffusion energy barriers mainly facilitate MnSe ⊂ 3DCNM-1.92 to exhibit high specific capacity, superior Li+ and electron transport kinetics.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Encapsulating MnSe Nanoparticles Inside 3D Hierarchical Carbon Frameworks with Lithium Storage Boosted by in Situ Electrochemical Phase Transformation</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Tao; Liu, Jianwen; Zhang, Manshu; Yang, Dexin; Zheng, Jianhui; Ju, Zhijin; Cheng, Jianlin; Zhuang, Jinyang; Liu, Yangai; Zhong, Jiasong; Liu, Hao; Wang, Guoxiu; Zheng, Rongkun; Guo, Zaiping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Electrode materials that act through the electrochem. conversion mechanism, such as metal selenides, have been considered as promising anode candidates for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), although their fast capacity attenuation and inadequate elec. cond. are impeding their practical application.  In this work, these issues are addressed through the efficient fabrication of MnSe nanoparticles inside porous carbon hierarchical architectures for evaluation as anode materials for LIBs.  D. functional theory simulations indicate that there is a completely irreversible phase transformation during the initial cycle, and the high structural reversibility of β-MnSe provides a low energy barrier for the diffusion of lithium ions.  Electron localization function calcns. demonstrate that the phase transformation leads to high charge transfer kinetics and a favorable lithium ion diffusion coeff.  Benefitting from the phase transformation and unique structural engineering, the MnSe/C chestnut-like structures with boosted cond. deliver enhanced lithium storage performance (885 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 0.2 A g-1 after 200 cycles), superior cycling stability (a capacity of 880 mA h g-1 at 1 A g-1 after 1000 cycles), and outstanding rate performance (416 mA h g-1 at 2 A g-1).</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref33" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1039/D0DT03540H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Polymerization inspired synthesis of MnO@carbon nanowires with long cycling stability for lithium ion battery anodes: growth mechanism and electrochemical performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Fang; Li, Shuangfu; Han, Kai; Li, Yajuan; Liu, You-Nian</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Dalton Transactions</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">50</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
