            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Manganese-based transition metal oxides are regarded as one kind of high capacity and low cost anode material for Li-ion batteries.  To overcome the challenges of poor elec. cond. and large volumetric expansion during the charging-discharging process of MnO, we here synthesize MnO@carbon (MnO@C) nanowires via the polymn. inspired in situ growth of [Mn-NTA] (NTA = nitrilotriacetic acid) precursor nanowires with a subsequent heat treatment process.  The growth mechanism of [Mn-NTA] precursor nanowires was studied.  The morphol. of the precursor nanowires depended largely on the molar ratio of MnCl2 to NTA reactants.  At a molar ratio of 2, the length of the [Mn-NTA] nanowires reached up to more than 140μm.  Furthermore, the as-synthesized MnO@C nanowires were integrated with a very low content of reduced graphene oxide (rGO) to prep. a self-standing paper-like MnO@C/rGO anode for lithium ion batteries without a binder.  The MnO@C/rGO anode showed a unique structure with one-dimensional porous MnO nanowires hierarchically encapsulated by a conductive carbon framework.  As a result, the self-standing electrode achieved a high capacity of 1368 mA h g-1 after 100 cycles at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1 and prominent cycling stability with a capacity of 689.9 mA h g-1 even after 1700 cycles at 2000 mA g -1.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref34" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1021/acs.nanolett.9b05349"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ou, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ultrahigh and durable volumetric lithium/sodium storage enabled by a highly dense graphene-encapsulated nitrogen-doped carbon@Sn compact monolith</span>. <i>Nano Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>20</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2034</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">2046</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acs.nanolett.9b05349</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D20%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D2034-2046%26journal%3DNano%2BLett.%26author%3DY.%2BLi%26author%3DC.%2BOu%26author%3DJ.%2BZhu%26author%3DZ.%2BLiu%26author%3DJ.%2BYu%26author%3DW.%2BLi%26author%3DH.%2BZhang%26author%3DQ.%2BZhang%26author%3DZ.%2BGuo%26title%3DUltrahigh%2Band%2Bdurable%2Bvolumetric%2Blithium%252Fsodium%2Bstorage%2Benabled%2Bby%2Ba%2Bhighly%2Bdense%2Bgraphene-encapsulated%2Bnitrogen-doped%2Bcarbon%2540Sn%2Bcompact%2Bmonolith%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facs.nanolett.9b05349&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.4c01408&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.9b05349&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrahigh and Durable Volumetric Lithium/Sodium Storage Enabled by a Highly Dense Graphene-Encapsulated Nitrogen-Doped Carbon@Sn Compact Monolith</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yunyong; Ou, Changzhi; Zhu, Junlu; Liu, Zhonggang; Yu, Jianlin; Li, Wenwu; Zhang, Haiyan; Zhang, Qiaobao; Guo, Zaiping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">20</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2034-2046</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Tin-based composites hold promise as anodes for high-capacity lithium/sodium-ion batteries (LIBs/SIBs); however, it is necessary to use carbon coated nanosized tin to solve the issues related to large vol. changes during electrochem. cycling, thus leading to the low volumetric capacity for tin-based composites due to their low packing d.  Herein, we design a highly dense graphene-encapsulated nitrogen-doped carbon@Sn (HD N-C@Sn/G) compact monolith with Sn nanoparticles double-encapsulated by N-C and graphene, which exhibits a high d. of 2.6 g cm-3 and a high cond. of 212 S m-1.  The as-obtained HD N-C@Sn/G monolith anode exhibits ultrahigh and durable volumetric lithium/sodium storage.  Specifically, it delivers a high volumetric capacity of 2692 mAh cm-3 after 100 cycles at 0.1 A g-1 and an ultralong cycling stability exceeding 1500 cycles at 1.0 A g-1 with only 0.019% capacity decay per cycle in lithium-ion batteries.  Besides, in situ TEM and ex situ SEM have revealed that the unique double-encapsulated structure effectively mitigates drastic vol. variation of the tin nanoparticles during electrode cycling.  Furthermore, the full cell using HD N-C@Sn/G as an anode and LiCoO2 as a cathode displays a superior cycling stability.  This work provides a new avenue and deep insight into the design of high-volumetric-capacity alloy-based anodes with ultralong cycle life.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref35" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2021.106897"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Template-directed synthesis of Co<sub>2</sub>P/MoSe<sub>2</sub> in a N-doped carbon hollow structure for efficient and stable sodium/potassium ion storage</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>93</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">106897</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.nanoen.2021.106897</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D93%26publication_year%3D2022%26journal%3DNano%2BEnergy%26author%3DY.%2BWang%26author%3DW.%2BKang%26author%3DX.%2BPu%26author%3DY.%2BLiang%26author%3DB.%2BXu%26author%3DX.%2BLu%26author%3DD.%2BSun%26author%3DY.%2BCao%26title%3DTemplate-directed%2Bsynthesis%2Bof%2BCo2P%252FMoSe2%2Bin%2Ba%2BN-doped%2Bcarbon%2Bhollow%2Bstructure%2Bfor%2Befficient%2Band%2Bstable%2Bsodium%252Fpotassium%2Bion%2Bstorage%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.nanoen.2021.106897&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.4c01408&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.nanoen.2021.106897&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Template-directed synthesis of Co2P/MoSe2 in a N-doped carbon hollow structure for efficient and stable sodium/potassium ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Yuyu; Kang, Wenpei; Pu, Xiangjun; Liang, Yucang; Xu, Ben; Lu, Xiaoqing; Sun, Daofeng; Cao, Yuliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">93</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">106897</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Multi-component hollow structures with attractive physicochem. properties, often show superior electrochem. performance in alkali-ion batteries.  Herein, a template-directed strategy is proposed for synthesis of multi-component hollow nanosphere with Co2P/MoSe2 confined in N-doped carbon (Co2P/MoSe2@NC).  This structure markedly improves the kinetics, provides sufficient active sites and accommodates vol. expansion, for the large-sized K+/Na+ storage, which is proved by the in-situ and ex-situ transmission electron microscopy measurements.  As for sodium storage, a capacity of 230 mAh g-1 over 1500 cycles can be retained at current of 2.0 A g-1, with a capacity retention of 83%.  In terms of K+ storage, Co2P/MoSe2@NC anodes display excellent rate capability and ultra-long cycling performance (177.6 mAh g-1 at 1.0 A g-1 for 5000 cycles with a capacity retention of 75%).  Based on the anal. of electrode process by comparison of dQ/dV curves and theor. calcns., the intercalation-conversion reaction for K+ storage is more reversible and the weaker adsorption of K+ on the Co2P/MoSe2 interface can guarantee the stable storage of the K+-ions.  High energy d. of 43.34 Wh kg-1 at power densities of 22263.7 W kg-1 is delivered in the Co2P/MoSe2@NC//AC potassium-ion hybrid supercapacitor.  This indicates that a selenide/phosphide combination can exert useful synergistic effects on the large-sized K+/Na+ storage, and is a promising anode candidate.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref36" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201808291"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Yolk–shell structured FeP@C nanoboxes as advanced anode materials for rechargeable lithium-/Potassium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Antimony Nanorod Encapsulated in Cross-Linked Carbon for High-Performance Sodium Ion Battery Anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cui, Chunyu; Xu, Jiantie; Zhang, Yiqiong; Wei, Zengxi; Mao, Minglei; Lian, Xin; Wang, Shuangyin; Yang, Chongyin; Fan, Xiulin; Ma, Jianmin; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">19</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">538-544</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony- (Sb) based materials have been considered as one of promising anodes for sodium ion batteries (SIBs) owing to their high theor. capacities and appropriate sodium inserting potentials.  So far, the reported energy d. and cycling stability of the Sb-based anodes for SIBs are quite limited and need to be significantly improved.  Here, we develop a novel Sb/C hybrid encapsulating the Sb nanorods into highly conductive N and S codoped carbon (Sb@(N, S-C)) frameworks.  As an anode for SIBs, the Sb@(N, S-C) hybrid maintains high reversible capacities of 621.1 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1 after 150 cycles, and 390.8 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1 after 1000 cycles.  At higher current densities of 2, 5, and 10 A g-1, the Sb@(N, S-C) hybrid also can display high reversible capacities of 534.4, 430.8, and 374.7 mAh g-1, resp.  Such impressive sodium storage properties are mainly attributed to the unique cross-linked carbon networks providing highly conductive frameworks for fast transfer of ions and electrons, alleviating the vol. expansion and preventing the agglomeration of Sb nanorods during the cycling.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref38" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1021/acssuschemeng.0c03273"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhan, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiao, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">rational design of N-doped CuS@C nanowires toward high-performance half/full sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>ACS Sustain. Chem.                 10.1021/acssuschemeng.0c03273</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D8%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D11317-11327%26journal%3DACS%2BSustain.%2BChem.%2BEng.%26author%3DD.%2BZhao%26author%3DM.%2BYin%26author%3DC.%2BFeng%26author%3DK.%2BZhan%26author%3DQ.%2BJiao%26author%3DH.%2BLi%26author%3DY.%2BZhao%26title%3Drational%2Bdesign%2Bof%2BN-doped%2BCuS%2540C%2Bnanowires%2Btoward%2Bhigh-performance%2Bhalf%252Ffull%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facssuschemeng.0c03273&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.4c01408&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facssuschemeng.0c03273&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="

                        cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ingeniously Designed Yolk-Shell-Structured FeSe2@NDC Nanoboxes as an Excellent Long-Life and High-Rate Anode for Half/Full Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Feng, Jian; Luo, Shao-hua; Zhan, Yang; Yan, Sheng-xue; Li, Peng-wei; Zhang, Lin; Wang, Qing; Zhang, Ya-hui; Liu, Xin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">43</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">51095-51106</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Thanks to their high cond. and theor. capacity, transition metal selenides have demanded significant research attention as prospective anodes for sodium-ion batteries.  Nevertheless, their practical applications are hindered by finite cycle life and inferior rate performance because of large vol. expansion, polyselenide dissoln., and sluggish dynamics.  Herein, the nitrogen-doped carbon (NC)-coated FeSe2 nanoparticles encapsulated in NC nanoboxes (termed FeSe2@NDC NBs) are fabricated through the facile thermal selenization of polydopamine-wrapped Prussian blue precursors.  In this composite, the existing nitrogen-doped dual carbon layer improves the intrinsic cond. and structural integrity, while the unique porous yolk-shell architecture significantly mitigates the vol. swelling during the sodium/desodium process.  Moreover, the derived Fe-N-C bonds can effectively capture polyselenide, as well as promote Na+ transportation and good reversible conversion reaction.  As expected, the FeSe2@NDC NBs deliver remarkable rate performance (374.9 mA h g-1 at 10.0 A g-1) and long-cycling stability (403.3 mA h g-1 over 2000 loops at 5.0 A g-1).  When further coupled with a self-made Na3V2(PO4)3@C cathode in sodium-ion full cells, FeSe2@NDC NBs also exhibit considerably high and stable sodium-storage performance.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref40" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2017.06.001"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lin, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ullah, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hai, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xin, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liao, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">NiS<sub>2</sub>@CoS<sub>2</sub> nanocrystals encapsulated in N-doped carbon nanocubes for high performance lithium/sodium ion batteries</span>. <i>Energy Storage Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>11</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">67</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">74</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rock-Salt MnS0.5Se0.5 Nanocubes Assembled on N-Doped Graphene Forming van der Waals Heterostructured Hybrids as High-Performance Anode for Lithium- and Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xing, Shiqi; Yang, Jing; Muska, Mairman; Li, Huanran; Yang, Qing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">19</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">22608-22620</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Manganese-based chalcogenides would be of latent capacity in serving as anodes for assembling lithium- and/or sodium-ion batteries (LIBs/SIBs) due to their large theor. capacity, low price, and low-toxicity functionality, while the low electrocond. and easy agglomeration behavior may impede their tech. applications.  Here, a solid-state soln. of MnS0.5Se0.5 nanocubes in rock-salt phase has been synthesized for the first time at a relatively low temp. from the precursors of Mn(II) acetylacetonate with dibenzyl dichalcogens in oleylamine with octadecene, and the MnS0.5Se0.5 nanocubes have been assembled with N-doped graphene to form a new kind of heterostructured nanohybrids (shortened as MnS0.5Se0.5/N-G hybrids), which are very potential for the fabrication of metal-ion batteries including LIBs and/or SIBs.  Investigations revealed that there have been dense vacancies generated and active sites increased via nonequil. alloying of MnS and MnSe into the solid-soln. MnS0.5Se0.5 nanocubes with segregation and defects achieved in the low-temp. soln. synthetic route.  Meanwhile, the introduction of N-doped graphene forming heterojunction interfaces between MnS0.5Se0.5 and N-doped graphene would efficiently enhance their electrocond. and avoid agglomeration of the active MnS0.5Se0.5 nanocubes with considerably improved electrochem. properties.  As a result, the MnS0.5Se0.5/N-G hybrids delivered superior Li/Na storage capacities with outstanding rate performance as well as satisfactorily lasting stability (1039/457 mA h g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 for LIBs/SIBs).  Addnl., full-cell LIBs of the anodic MnS0.5Se0.5/N-G constructed with cathodic LiFePO4 (LFP) further confirmed the promising future for their practical application.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref43" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1007/s40195-021-01200-w"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Niu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Controlled synthesis and Raman study of a 2D antiferromagnetic P-type semiconductor: α-MnSe</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Ningning; Zhu, Leilei; Shang, Honghui; Wang, Feng; Zhang, Yu; Yao, Yuyu; Wang, Junjun; Zhan, Xueying; Wang, Fengmei; He, Jun; Wang, Zhenxing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">14</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Two-dimensional (2D) non-van der Waals magnetic materials have attracted considerable attention due to their high-temp. ferromagnetism, active surface/interface properties originating from dangling bonds, and good stability under ambient conditions.  Here, we demonstrate the controlled synthesis and systematic Raman investigation of ultrathin non-van der Waals antiferromagnetic α-MnSe single crystals.  Square and triangular nanosheets with different growth orientations can be achieved by introducing different precursors via the atm. chem. vapor deposition (APCVD) method.  The temp.-dependent resonant enhancement in the Raman intensity of two peaks at 233.8 cm-1 and 459.9 cm-1 gives obvious evidence that the antiferromagnetic spin-ordering is below TN ∼160 K.  Besides, a new peak located at 254.2 cm-1, gradually appearing as the temp. decreased from 180 K to 100 K, may also be a signature of phase transition from paramagnetic to antiferromagnetic.  The phonon dispersion spectra of α-MnSe simulated by d. functional perturbation theory (DFPT) match well with the obsd. Raman signals.  Moreover, a fabricated α-MnSe phototransistor exhibits p-type conducting behavior and high photodetection performance.  We believe that these findings will be beneficial for the applications of 2D α-MnSe in magnetic and semiconducting fields.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref45" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1002/smm2.1084"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zou, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tian, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lv, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kutty, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hong, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Controlled growth of ultrathin ferromagnetic β-MnSe semiconductor</span>. <i>SmartMater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>3</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">482</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">490</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Encapsulating MnSe Nanoparticles Inside 3D Hierarchical Carbon Frameworks with Lithium Storage Boosted by in Situ Electrochemical Phase Transformation</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Tao; Liu, Jianwen; Zhang, Manshu; Yang, Dexin; Zheng, Jianhui; Ju, Zhijin; Cheng, Jianlin; Zhuang, Jinyang; Liu, Yangai; Zhong, Jiasong; Liu, Hao; Wang, Guoxiu; Zheng, Rongkun; Guo, Zaiping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Electrode materials that act through the electrochem. conversion mechanism, such as metal selenides, have been considered as promising anode candidates for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), although their fast capacity attenuation and inadequate elec. cond. are impeding their practical application.  In this work, these issues are addressed through the efficient fabrication of MnSe nanoparticles inside porous carbon hierarchical architectures for evaluation as anode materials for LIBs.  D. functional theory simulations indicate that there is a completely irreversible phase transformation during the initial cycle, and the high structural reversibility of β-MnSe provides a low energy barrier for the diffusion of lithium ions.  Electron localization function calcns. demonstrate that the phase transformation leads to high charge transfer kinetics and a favorable lithium ion diffusion coeff.  Benefitting from the phase transformation and unique structural engineering, the MnSe/C chestnut-like structures with boosted cond. deliver enhanced lithium storage performance (885 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 0.2 A g-1 after 200 cycles), superior cycling stability (a capacity of 880 mA h g-1 at 1 A g-1 after 1000 cycles), and outstanding rate performance (416 mA h g-1 at 2 A g-1).</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref47" class="refNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit47" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2020.135783"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mi, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, W.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Se-C bond and reversible SEI in facile synthesized SnSe<sub>2</sub>⊂3D carbon induced stable anode for sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Electrochim.                         cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Se-C bond and reversible SEI in facile synthesized SnSe2⊂3D carbon induced stable anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Kaiwei; Zhang, Xixue; Song, Keming; Zhang, Jiyu; Liu, Chuntai; Mi, Liwei; Wang, Yingying; Chen, Weihua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">337</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metal selenides have gained great attention and are considered as one of promising anode materials for resource-abundant Na-ion batteries, due to their high capacity and higher reaction kinetics.  However, poor cycling hinders their practical applications.  To solve the issue, effective combining rationally designed functional C architecture and metal selenides is advanced expectedly, yet complex routines are inevitable and severely impede further engineering prodn.  Herein, with a facile, environmental-friendly, easy-scalable integrated carbo-thermal method, SnSe2 nanoparticles are well-embedded in 3-dimensional porous C (SnSe2⊂3DC).  The inherent Se-C bond and electrochem. formed reversible solid electrolyte interphase cooperating with the buffering 3-dimensional porous structure successfully endow stable structure and high reversible conversion and alloying reactions.  As a result, the obtained SnSe2⊂3DC delivers excellent capacity of 340 mAh g-1 without decay after 170 cycles at high c.d. of 2.5 A g-1.  The full cell SnSe2⊂3DC//NaFePO4 was assembled to confirm its applications.  This work could not only provide easy-scalable high-performance anode for SIBs applications but also open avenue to promote other electrode materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref48" class="refNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit48" data-doi="10.1038/s41467-019-08506-5"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lin, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, D. Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Evolution of the electrochemical interface in sodium ion batteries with ether electrolytes</span>. <i>Nat. Commun.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>10</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">725</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1038/s41467-019-08506-5</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D10%26publication_year%3D2019%26pages%3D725%26journal%3DNat.%2BCommun.%26author%3DK.%2BLi%26author%3DJ.%2BZhang%26author%3DD.%2BLin%26author%3DD.%2BW.%2BWang%26author%3DB.%2BLi%26author%3DW.%2BLv%26author%3DS.%2BSun%26author%3DY.%2BB.%2BHe%26author%3DF.%2BKang%26author%3DQ.%2BH.%2BYang%26author%3DL.%2BZhou%26author%3DT.%2BY.%2BZhang%26title%3DEvolution%2Bof%2Bthe%2Belectrochemical%2Binterface%2Bin%2Bsodium%2Bion%2Bbatteries%2Bwith%2Bether%2Belectrolytes%26doi%3D10.1038%252Fs41467-019-08506-5&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.4c01408&amp;doiOfLink=10.1038%2Fs41467-019-08506-5&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Evolution of the electrochemical interface in sodium ion batteries with ether electrolytes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Kaikai; Zhang, Jun; Lin, Dongmei; Wang, Da-Wei; Li, Baohua; Lv, Wei; Sun, Sheng; He, Yan-Bing; Kang, Feiyu; Yang, Quan-Hong; Zhou, Limin; Zhang, Tong-Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">725</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NCAOBW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2041-1723</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Research</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Ether based electrolytes have surfaced as alternatives to conventional carbonates allowing for enhanced electrochem. performance of sodium-ion batteries; however, the primary source of the improvement remains poorly understood.  Here we show that coupling titanium dioxide and other anode materials with diglyme does enable higher efficiency and reversible capacity than those for the combination involving ester electrolytes.  Importantly, the electrolyte dependent performance is revealed to be the result of the different structural evolution induced by a varied sodiation depth.  A suit of characterizations show that the energy barrier to charge transfer at the interface between electrolyte and electrode is the factor that dominates the interfacial electrochem. characteristics and therefore the energy storage properties.  Our study proposes a reliable parameter to assess the intricate sodiation dynamics in sodium-ion batteries and could guide the design of aprotic electrolytes for next generation rechargeable batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref49" class="refNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit49" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.1c21934"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qin, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zeng, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dai, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Constructing heterostructured bimetallic selenides on an N-doped carbon nanoframework as anodes for ultrastable Na-ion batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>14</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1222</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1232</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsami.1c21934</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D14%26publication_year%3D2022%26pages%3D1222-1232%26journal%3DACS%2BAppl.%2BMater.%2BInterfaces%26author%3DF.%2BHuang%26author%3DL.%2BWang%26author%3DD.%2BQin%26author%3DZ.%2BXu%26author%3DM.%2BJin%26author%3DY.%2BChen%26author%3DX.%2BZeng%26author%3DZ.%2BDai%26title%3DConstructing%2Bheterostructured%2Bbimetallic%2Bselenides%2Bon%2Ban%2BN-doped%2Bcarbon%2Bnanoframework%2Bas%2Banodes%2Bfor%2Bultrastable%2BNa-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsami.1c21934&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.4c01408&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsami.1c21934&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Constructing Heterostructured Bimetallic Selenides on an N-Doped Carbon Nanoframework as Anodes for Ultrastable Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Fei; Wang, Lei; Qin, Decai; Xu, Zhibin; Jin, Meiqi; Chen, Yu; Zeng, Xianxiang; Dai, Zhihui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1222-1232</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition-metal selenides have been recognized as a class of promising anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) on account of their high capacity.  Nevertheless, the sluggish conversion kinetics and rapid capacity decay caused by insufficient cond. and vol. change restrain their applications.  Herein, hollow heterostructured bimetallic selenides embedded in an N-doped carbon nanoframework (H-CoSe2/ZnSe@NC) were prepd. via a facile template-engaged method.  Benefiting from the rich defect at the phase boundary of the CoSe2/ZnSe heterostructure, pre-reserved cavity, and enhanced structure rigidity, the abovementioned issues are resolved at once, and the accelerated charge transportation kinetics traced by spectroscopy techniques and theor. calcns. certify the interface effect in the capacity release.  In addn., ex situ XPS, X-ray diffraction, and high-resoln. transmission electron microscopy all confirm the high-reversible electrochem. conversion mechanism in H-CoSe2/ZnSe@NC.  Together with a reasonable structural architecture and the highly reversible conversion reaction, H-CoSe2/ZnSe@NC displays a prominent rate capacity (244.8 mA h g-1 at 10 A g-1) as well as an ultralong lifespan (10,000 cycles at 10 A g-1), highlighting the significance of structure control in fabricating high-performance anodes for SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref50" class="refNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit50" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA01946G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/C synthesized by a facile solid-phase method assisted with agarose as a high-performance cathode for sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>J. Mater. Chem. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>5</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">10261</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">10268</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C7TA01946G</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D5%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D10261-10268%26journal%3DJ.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%26author%3DP.%2BFeng%26author%3DW.%2BWang%26author%3DK.%2BWang%26author%3DS.%2BCheng%26author%3DK.%2BJiang%26title%3DNa3V2%2528PO4%25293%252FC%2Bsynthesized%2Bby%2Ba%2Bfacile%2Bsolid-phase%2Bmethod%2Bassisted%2Bwith%2Bagarose%2Bas%2Ba%2Bhigh-performance%2Bcathode%2Bfor%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC7TA01946G&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.4c01408&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC7TA01946G&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na3V2(PO4)3/C synthesized by a facile solid-phase method assisted with agarose as a high-performance cathode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Feng, Pingyuan; Wang, Wei; Wang, Kangli; Cheng, Shijie; Jiang, Kai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">21</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">10261-10268</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A type of Na3V2(PO4)3/C (NVP/C) cathode material for sodium ion batteries was synthesized via a facile solid-phase method.  Agarose, a natural polysaccharide from seaweed that can form a 3D network structure through hydrogen bonds in polar solvents, was used as a carbon source and a medium to form NVP/C particles as nanograins with a thin layer of carbon coating in a 3D carbon network.  As the cathode, the NVP/C material exhibited a reversible capacity of 116 mA h g-1 at 1C, which is very close to its theor. capacity (117.6 mA h g-1), with a capacity retention of 97.3% after 500 cycles.  At 20C, the NVP/C had a capacity of 100 mA h g-1 and still kept a relatively stable capacity of 78 mA h g-1 after being cycled 7000 times.  Based on the excellent performance of the obtained cathode material, a sodium ion full cell was assembled with S-doped carbon as the anode, which delivered 110 mA h g-1 of discharge capacity at 200 mA h g-1 (calcd. using NVP as the cathode) and displayed an av. voltage of around 1.7 V.  All of these results imply that the prepd. NVP/C has potential for application in sodium ion batteries for large-scale energy storage.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></div><script type="text/javascript" nonce="93187f3f89a3075b-SJC">window.refViewer={'ref1':['cit1'],'ref2':['cit2'],'ref3':['cit3'],'ref4':['cit4'],'ref5':['cit5'],'ref6':['cit6'],'ref7':['cit7'],'ref8':['cit8'],'ref9':['cit9'],'ref10':['cit10'],'ref11':['cit11'],'ref12':['cit12'],'ref13':['cit13'],'ref14':['cit14'],'ref15':['cit15'],'ref16':['cit16'],'ref17':['cit17'],'ref18':['cit18'],'ref19':['cit19'],'ref20':['cit20'],'ref21':['cit21'],'ref22':['cit22'],'ref23':['cit23'],'ref24':['cit24'],'ref25':['cit25'],'ref26':['cit26'],'ref27':['cit27'],'ref28':['cit28'],'ref29':['cit29'],'ref30':['cit30'],'ref31':['cit31'],'ref32':['cit32'],'ref33':['cit33'],'ref34':['cit34'],'ref35':['cit35'],'ref36':['cit36'],'ref37':['cit37'],'ref38':['cit38'],'ref39':['cit39'],'ref40':['cit40'],'ref41':['cit41'],'ref42':['cit42'],'ref43':['cit43'],'ref44':['cit44'],'ref45':['cit45'],'ref46':['cit46'],'ref47':['cit47'],'ref48':['cit48'],'ref49':['cit49'],'ref50':['cit50']}</script><div class="articleCitedByDropzone" data-pb-dropzone="articleCitedByDropzone"><div class="cited-by"><div class="article_content-header cited-content_header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div tabindex="0" class="article_content-title"><h2 id="citeThis">Cited By</h2><div class="article__copy"> <button class="article__copy__btn"><i aria-hidden="true" class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><div class="cited-by__content"><div class="sciteMetricsDropzone">

        </p><ol id="rightTab-references" class="useLabel"><li id="rightTab-ref1"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref1" class="rightTabRefNumLink">1</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit1" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.0c08818"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tan, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Q.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">FeSe<sub>2</sub>@C microrods as a superior long-life and high-rate anode for sodium ion batteries</span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>14</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">17683</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">17692</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsnano.0c08818</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">FeSe2@C Microrods as a Superior Long-Life and High-Rate Anode for Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pan, Qichang; Zhang, Man; Zhang, Lixuan; Li, Yahao; Li, Yu; Tan, Chunlei; Zheng, Fenghua; Huang, Youguo; Wang, Hongqiang; Li, Qingyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">17683-17692</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition-metal selenides have emerged as promising anode materials for sodium ion batteries (SIBs).  Nevertheless, they suffer from vol. expansion, polyselenide dissoln., and sluggish kinetics, which lead to inadequate conversion reaction toward sodium and poor reversibility during the desodiation process.  Therefore, the transition-metal selenides are far from long cycling stability, outstanding rate performance, and high initial Coulombic efficiency, which are the major challenges for practical application in SIBs.  Here, an efficient anode material including an FeSe2 core and N-doped carbon shell with inner void space as well as high cond. is developed for outstanding rate performance and long cycle life SIBs.  In the ingeniously designed FeSe2@NC microrods, the N-doped carbon shell can facilitate mass transport/electron transfer, protect the FeSe2 core from the electrolyte, and accommodate vol. variation of FeSe2 with the help of the inner void of the core.  Thus, the FeSe2@NC microrods can maintain strong structural integrity upon long cycling and ensure a good reversible conversion reaction of FeSe2 during the discharge/charge process.  As a result, the as-prepd. FeSe2@NC microrods exhibit excellent sodium storage performance and ultrahigh stability, achieving an excellent rate capability (411 mAh g-1 at 10.0 A g-1) and a long-term cycle performance (401.3 mAh g-1 after 2000 cycles at 5.0 A g-1).</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1002/anie.202004914"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zeng, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Enhanced multiple anchoring and catalytic conversion of polysulfides by amorphous MoS<sub>3</sub> nanoboxes for high-performance Li-S batteries</span>. <i>Angew. Chem., Int. Ed</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>59</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">13071</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">13078</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/anie.202004914</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The practical implementation of lithium-sulfur batteries is obstructed by poor cond., sluggish redox kinetics, the shuttle effect, large vol. variation, and low areal loading of sulfur electrodes.  Now, amorphous N-doped carbon/MoS3 (NC/MoS3) nanoboxes with hollow porous architectures have been meticulously designed as an advanced sulfur host.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The exploration of next-generation sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) is a worldwide concern to replace the current com. lithium-ion batteries, mitigating the increasing exhaustion of Li resources.  Sodium transition metal oxides are considered to be one of the most promising cathode materials for SIBs.  The anionic redox reaction in Li-rich transition metal oxides is capable of providing extra capacity in addn. to the cationic redox activities in lithium-ion batteries.  A similar phenomenon exists in SIBs, which even applies to Na-deficient transition metal oxides.  Moreover, transition metal oxides with mixed phase also demonstrate great potential.  In this review, studies on anionic redox are first systematically introduced.  The up-to-date advances on high-capacity transition metal oxide cathode materials for SIBs are then classified and summarized in different groups assocd. with or without anionic redox.  The existing challenges as well as available solns. and strategies are discussed, and proposals with new insights are made at the end.  It is expected that this work can provide new perspectives on controlling the anionic redox activity and finding novel high-capacity oxide cathode materials for SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1021/acs.nanolett.8b05189"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xue, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ren, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Rayleigh-instability-induced bismuth nanorod@nitrogen-doped carbon nanotubes as a long cycling and high rate anode for sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Nano Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>19</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1998</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">2004</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Constructing a heterojunction and introducing an interfacial interaction by designing ideal structures have the inherent advantages of optimizing electronic structures and macroscopic mech. properties.         </div><div class="casAbstract">FeS2 as a sodium-ion battery anode material has attracted great attention on account of its high theor. capacity, abundance, low cost, and other advantages.  However, the poor elec. cond. of FeS2 and the huge vol. expansion in the sodium-ion insertion/extn. process are the key factors affecting its electrochem. performance.  Herein, NaCl was used as a template to successfully synthesize a composite material of a nitrogen-doped porous carbon framework loaded with ultrafine FeS2 nanoparticles (FeS2/NPCF).  The three-dimensional porous carbon framework improves the cond. of the material as well as effectively suppresses the vol. expansion of the material during the charge and discharge process, thus improving the cycle performance of the composite material.  In the three-dimensional porous carbon framework with a larger sp. surface area, ultrafine FeS2 particles can lessen the diffusion distance and enhance the Na+ diffusion rate.  The ultrafine FeS2 nanoparticles loaded on the nitrogen-doped highly conductive porous carbon framework reduce the e-transport resistance and limit the vol. change of FeS2 during the cycle, which improves the structure's stability.  These advantages make FeS2/NPCF an ideal anode electrode material of a sodium-ion battery that shows excellent sodium storage performance.  A reversible capacity of 552 mAh g-1 is maintained with a capacity retention of 87% at 0.5A g-1 after 100 cycles.  Remarkably, even at 5A g-1, the FeS2/NPCF electrode still delivers a discharge capacity of 430 mAh g-1after 500 cycles.  FeS2/NPCF, with its excellent electrochem. performance, is considered a potential anode material for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref9" class="rightTabRefNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit9" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201807753"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mohrhusen, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ali, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chung, K.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Molybedenum disulfide (MoS2) is regarded as a promising anode material for next-generation sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) owing to its high theor. capacity.  However, its low cond., large vol. changes, and undesirable phase transformation hinder its practical applications.  In this study, we synthesize a hierarchically designed core-shell heterostructure based on nitrogen-doped MoS2/C and silicon oxycarbide (SiOC) (N-MoS2/C@SiOC) via the facile pyrolysis of a suspension of an N-MoS2/polyfurfural precursor in silicone oil.  The in situ nitrogen doping in a two-dimensional MoS2 structure with carbon incorporation leads to the enlargement of the interlayer spacing and enhancement of the electronic cond. and mech. stability, which allows the facile, highly reversible insertion and extn. of sodium ions upon cycling.  Further, the nanoscale SiOC shell with surface capacitive reactivity provides a conductive pathway, preventing unfavorable side reactions at the electrode/electrolyte interface and acting as a structure-reinforcing buffer against severe vol. expansion issues.  As a result, the N-MoS2/C@SiOC composite exhibits high reversible capacity (540.7 mAh g-1), high-capacity retention (&gt;100% after 200 cycles), and excellent rate capability up to 10 A g-1.  The simple hierarchical core-shell design strategy developed in this study allows for the fabrication of high-performance metal sulfide anodes as well as other high-capacity anode materials for energy storage applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref12" class="rightTabRefNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit12" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201706317"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, D.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Abstr.: MXenes have attracted increasing attention because of their rich surface functional groups, high elec. cond., and outstanding dispersibility in many solvents, and have demonstrated competitive efficiency in energy storage and conversion applications.  However, the restacking nature of MXene nanosheets like other two-dimensional (2D) materials through van der Waals forces results in sluggish ionic kinetics, restricted no. of active sites, and ultimate deterioration of MXene material/device performance.  The strategy of raising 2D MXenes into three-dimensional (3D) structures has been considered an efficient way for reducing restacking, providing greater porosity, higher surface area, and shorter distances for mass transport of ions, surpassing std. one-dimensional (1D) and 2D structures.  In multivalent ion batteries, the pos. multivalent ions combine with two or more electrons at the same time, so their capacities are two or three times that of lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) under the same conditions, e.g., a magnesium ion battery has a high theor. specific capacity of 2 205 mAh g-1 and a high volumetric capacity of 3 833 mAh cm-3.  In this review, we summarize the most recent strategies for fabricating 3D MXene architectures, such as assembly, template, 3D printing, electrospinning, aerogel, and gas foaming methods.  Special consideration has been given to the applications of highly porous 3D MXenes in energy storage devices beyond LIBs, such as sodium ion batteries (SIBs), potassium ion batteries (KIBs), magnesium ion batteries (MIBs), zinc ion batteries (ZIBs), and aluminum ion batteries (AIBs).  Finally, the authors provide a summary of the future opportunities and challenges for the construction of 3D MXenes and MXene-based electrodes for applications beyond LIBs.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The fundamental understanding of sodium storage mechanisms in amorphous carbon is essential to develop high-performance anode materials for sodium-ion batteries.  However, the intrinsic relation between the structure of amorphous carbon and Na+ storage remains to be debated due to the difficulty in controlling and characterizing the local at. configurations of amorphous carbon.  Here we report quant. measurements of Na+ storage in a low-temp. dealloyed hard carbon with a tunable local structure from completely disordered micropores to gradually increased graphitic order domains.  The structure-capacity-potential correlation not only verifies the disputing "adsorption-intercalation" mechanisms, i.e., Na+ intercalation into local graphitic domains for the low-voltage plateaus and adsorption in fully disordered carbon for the sloping voltage profiles, but also unveils a new mechanism of Na+ adsorption on defective sites of graphitic carbon in the medium-potential sloping region.  The quant. investigations provide essential insights into the reaction mechanisms of Na+ with amorphous carbon for designing advanced sodium-ion battery anodes.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref19" class="rightTabRefNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit19" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202003911"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lai, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ultrahigh phosphorus doping of carbon for high-rate sodium ion batteries anode</span>. <i>Adv.                 10.1002/aenm.202003911</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrahigh Phosphorus Doping of Carbon for High-Rate Sodium Ion Batteries Anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yan, Jie; Li, Haomiao; Wang, Kangli; Jin, Qianzheng; Lai, Chenglong; Wang, Ruxing; Cao, Shengling; Han, Jing; Zhang, Zhuchan; Su, Jinzhao; Jiang, Kai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">21</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2003911</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Phosphorus doped carbons are of particular interest as anode materials because of their large interlayer spacing and strong adsorption of Na+ ions.  However, it remains challenging to achieve high phosphorus doping due to the limited choices of phosphorus sources and the difficulty in constructing oxygen-free synthesis system.  Herein, a new synthesis strategy is proposed to prep. ultrahigh phosphorus-doped carbon (UPC) anodes for high performance sodium ion batteries (SIBs).  By using two commonly available, miscible, evaporable liqs. in PCl3 and C6H12, as phosphorus and carbon sources, an oxygen-free reaction system is successfully established by N2 bubbling to simultaneously realize carbonization and in situ P doping.  The P content can reach 30 wt%, much higher than most reported P-doping carbon-based materials.  Furthermore, the doped P is dominated by substitutional P-(C3) protrusions in the carbon lattice, which can significantly enlarge the interlayer spacing and enhance the adsorption energy of Na+.  When serving as the SIBs anode, the UPC delivers an ultrahigh reversible capacity of 510.4 mAh g-1 with a rational operating voltage of 0.54 V, and the best rate capability of 397.1 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1.  This new strategy will effectively promote the practical application of hard carbon.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref20" class="rightTabRefNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit20" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201606023"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Noonan, O.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Tailored yolk-shell Sn@C nanoboxes for high-performance lithium storage</span>. <i>Adv.                         rightTab-cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Microsized Gray Tin as a High-Rate and Long-Life Anode Material for Advanced Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Yansong; Yao, Qian; Shao, Ruiwen; Wang, Cheng; Yan, Weishan; Ma, Jizhen; Liu, Duo; Yang, Jian; Qian, Yitai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are developed to address the serious concern about the limited resources of lithium.  To achieve high energy d., anode materials with a large specific capacity and a low operation voltage are highly desirable.  Herein, microsized particles of gray Sn (α-Sn) are explored as an anode material of SIBs for the first time.  The distinct structure of α-Sn endows it the reduced vol. change, the improved interaction with polymer binders and the in situ formation of amorphous Sn, as supported by in situ XRD, TEM and DFT calcns.  Therefore, α-Sn exhibits an excellent electrochem. performance, much better than β-Sn widely used before.  Even microsized particles of α-Sn without any treatments deliver a capacity of ~ 451 mAh g-1 after 3500 cycles at 2 A g-1 or ~ 464 mAh g-1 at 4 A g-1 in a rate test.  The results indicate the promising potential of α-Sn in SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref22" class="rightTabRefNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit22" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2019.07.017"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, D.                         rightTab-cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical porous Co0.85Se@reduced graphene oxide ultrathin nanosheets with vacancy-enhanced kinetics as superior anodes for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Yongxin; Wang, Ziheng; Jiang, Ying; Li, Shuaijie; Li, Zehua; Zhang, Haiqin; Wu, Feng; Xie, Man; Li, Li; Chen, Renjie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metal selenides have received much attention from the rechargeable battery community owing to their considerable capacity.  However, attainment of a long cycle life and fast Na+ storage kinetics are still needed to enable their practical application.  Co0.85Se nanosheets prepd. using a simple hydrothermal method exhibit a hierarchical porous structure, which is conducive to fast electrolyte transport and rapid adsorption of Na+ ions.  Herein, to improve the electronic cond. of Co0.85Se, reduced graphene oxide (rGO) is introduced to construct a three-dimensional network and achieve fast electronic transport.  This defect-controlled Co0.85Se@rGO anode exhibits a highly reversible capacity of 460 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 0.5 A g-1.  Outstanding durability and remarkable rate stability are also achieved via the synergistic effects of vacancy transport and the heterostructure between Co0.85Se and rGO.  Furthermore, the Na+ insertion/extn. mechanism is systematically investigated using ex situ X-ray diffraction, Raman spectroscopy, high-resoln. transmission electron microscopy, and a series of electrochem. analyses.  These analyses enable detailed characterization of the ionic diffusion kinetics and corresponding components and structural changes.  Finally, a first-principles approach is employed to det. the diffusion energy barrier of Na+ ions in perfect CoSe and defective Co0.85Se.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref24" class="rightTabRefNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit24" data-doi="10.1002/smll.202004580"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Willow-leaf-like ZnSe@N-doped carbon nanoarchitecture as a stable and high-performance anode material for sodium-ion and potassium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>16</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">2004580</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">ZnSe is regarded as a promising anode material for energy storage due to its high theor. capacity and environment friendliness.  Nevertheless, it is still a significant challenge to obtain superior electrode materials with stable performance owing to the serious vol. change and aggregation upon cycling.  Herein, a willow-leaf-like N-doped C-coated ZnSe (ZnSe@NC) composite synthesized through facile solvothermal and subsequent selenization process is beneficial to expose more active sites and facilitate the fast electron/ion transmission.  These merits significantly enhance the electrochem. performances of ZnSe@NC for Na-ion batteries (SIBs) and K-ion batteries (PIBs).  The obtained ZnSe@NC exhibits outstanding rate performance (440.3 mA-h g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 and 144.4 mA-h g-1 at 10 A g-1) and ultralong cycle stability (242.2 mA-h g-1 at 8.0 A g-1 even after 3200 cycles) for SIBs. and 106.5 mA-h g-1 can be retained after 550 cycles and 71.4 mA-h g-1 is still remained after 1500 cycles at 200 mA g-1 when applied as anode for PIBs, indicating good cycle stability of the electrode.  The possible electrochem. mechanism and the ionic diffusion kinetics of the ZnSe@NC are studied using ex situ x-ray diffraction, high-resoln. TEM, and electrochem. analyses.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref25" class="rightTabRefNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit25" data-doi="10.1039/C8TA03967D"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, D.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Coaxial nanotubes are a significant class of nanoscale building blocks for advanced electrodes of secondary batteries.  Herein, one-dimensional (1D) coaxial double nanotubes (DNTs) consisting of α-MnSe inner tubes and N-doped carbon (N-C) outer tubes (abbreviated as α-MnSe@N-C DNTs) are successfully prepd. and are demonstrated to be promising anode material for Li-ion and Na-ion batteries (LIBs/NIBs). In addn., the outer N-C nanotube can effectively protect the active α-MnSe inner nanotube to realize such outstanding electrochem. properties owing to the high elec. cond. and particular 1D coaxial nanoarchitecture of the inner nanotube.  Moreover, α-MnSe@N-C DNTs also exhibit excellent Li/Na-storage properties and full-cell performances when coupled with com.         </div><div class="casAbstract">MnSe with high theor. capacity and reversibility is considered as a promising material for the anode of sodium ion batteries.  In this study, MnSe nanoparticles embedded in 1D carbon nanofibers (MnSe-NC) are successfully prepd. via facile electrospinning and subsequent selenization.  A carbon framework can effectively protect MnSe dispersed in it from agglomeration and can accommodate vol. variation in the conversion reaction between MnSe and Na+ to guarantee cycling stability.  The 1D fiber structure can increase the area of contact between electrode and electrolyte to shorten the diffusion path of Na+ and facilitate its transfer.  According to the kinetic anal., the storage process of sodium by MnSe-NC is a surface pseudocapacitive-controlled process with promising rate capability.  Impressively, An MnSe-NC anode in sodium ion full cells is investigated by pairing with an Na3V2(PO4)2@rGO cathode, which exhibits a reversible capacity of 195 mA h g-1 at 0.1 A g-1.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref27" class="rightTabRefNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit27" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.1c03056"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Niu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.                         rightTab-cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Bilateral Interfaces in In2Se3-CoIn2-CoSe2 Heterostructures for High-Rate Reversible Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiao, Shuhao; Li, Xinyan; Zhang, Wensi; Xiang, Yong; Li, Tingshuai; Niu, Xiaobin; Chen, Jun Song; Yan, Qingyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
